If you do not have one, you can create a Recruitee account at auth.recruitee.com/sign-up.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Recruitee to Make\n\nTo connect your Recruitee account to Make you need to obtain the API Token from your Recruitee account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your Recruitee account.\n\nClick Settings > Personal API Tokens > New Token.\n\nEnter a name for the token and click Save.\n\nAuthenticate by entering your Recruitee's account password and click Continue.\n\nCopy the Access Token to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the Recruitee module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Token field, enter the token details copied in step 5.\n\nIn the Company ID field, enter your company ID with which you want to establish a connection. You can find the Company ID at Settings > Personal API Tokens.\n\nClick Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nCandidates\nWatch Candidates\nWatch Requalified Candidates\nWatch Disqualified Candidates\nList Candidates\nGet a Candidate\nCreate a Candidate\nUpdate a Candidate\nDelete a Candidate\nTags\nList Tags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nNotes\nList Notes\nCreate Note\nUpdate Note\nDelete Note\nOffers\nList Offers\nGet an Offer\nCreate an Offer\nUpdate an Offer\nDelete an Offer\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Offers\nRecruitee\nGetting Started with Recruitee\nConnecting Recruitee to Make\nCandidates\nWatch Candidates\nWatch Requalified Candidates\nWatch Disqualified Candidates\nList Candidates\nGet a Candidate\nCreate a Candidate\nUpdate a Candidate\nDelete a Candidate\nTags\nList Tags\nCreate a Tag\nUpdate a Tag\nDelete a Tag\nNotes\nList Notes\nCreate Note\nUpdate Note\nDelete Note\nOffers\nList Offers\nGet an Offer\nCreate an Offer\nUpdate an Offer\nDelete an Offer\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Offers\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

      "title": "Greenhouse Recruiting",
      "url": "https://www.make.com/en/help/apps/hr-management/greenhouse",
      "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and ERPs\nCommerce\nCommunication\nCRM and Sales tools\nCustomer Support\nDatabase\nEducation\nFile and Document Management\nHR management\n4leads\nBambooHR\nBonusly\nDeel\nFactorial\nGreenhouse Recruiting\nHiBob\nOracle Fusion Cloud HCM\nPeople HR\nPersonio\nRecruitee\nServiceM8\nTestGorilla\nToggl Hire\nTrainual\nWeekdone\nWorkday Human Capital Management\nZoho Recruit\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsHR managementGreenhouse Recruiting\nGreenhouse Recruiting\n\nWith Greenhouse Recruiting modules in Make, you can watch and search for applications, candidates, jobs, job posts, and offers, add applications to, create, and update prospects and candidates, add attachments to applications and candidates, retrieve jobs and job posts, list approval flows, and add candidate notes in your Greenhouse Recruiting account.\n\nMake currently supports Greenhouse Recruiting, Greenhouse Onboarding is not supported at this time.\n\nTo get started with Greenhouse Recruiting, create an account at greenhouse.com.\n\nRequirements\n\nGreenhouse Recruiting: The account setting up the integration must have Developer Permissions in Greenhouse Recruiting.\n\nMake: To use Greenhouse Recruiting in Make, you must have the Make Enterprise plan. All Enterprise apps are currently labeled as premium tier 3 in Make.\n\nConnect Greenhouse Recruiting to Make\n\nTo connect your Greenhouse Recruiting account to Make, you must first create a Harvest API Key in your Greenhouse Recruiting account. The Greenhouse Recruiting account must have developer permissions to create an API key.\n\nNote on API key permissions\n\nGreenhouse Recruiting allows you to select specific permissions for each API key. We recommend to only select the permissions that correspond to the actions you want Make to perform in a specific scenario.\n\nDifferent scenarios may require different permissions based on the actions the scenario performs and the data the scenario works with. We recommend to create a separate API key and a separate connection for each scenario and include only the permissions that the specific scenario needs.\n\nTo create the connection:\n\nLog in to your Greenhouse Recruiting account.\n\nClick the Configure symbol > Dev Center.\n\nClick on API Credential Management.\n\nClick on Create new API key and enter the details below. Then click Manage permissions.\n\nAPI type\n\n\t\n\nHarvest\n\n\n\n\nPartner\n\n\t\n\nMake\n\n\n\n\nDescription\n\n\t\n\nInsert a description detailing what actions the API key is allowed to perform and permission information. The description will allow you to identify the purpose of the API keys for different scenarios. We recommend using the following format: Make API Key - [permissions].\n\nFor example: Make API Key - Delete, Edit, Add Candidate.\n\nCopy the API key to your clipboard, store it in a safe place as you are only able to view your API key once, and click I have stored the API key.\n\nSelect only the permissions that your scenario will require in the Manage permissions section and click Save. Refer to the module list below to identify the required permissions for each module.\n\nLog in to your Make account and add a Greenhouse Recruiting module to a scenario.\n\nClick Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, you will first be prompted to create a Webhook. Click Create a webhook > Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nPaste the API key copied in step 5 in the API Key field and click Save.\n\nIf you receive the following error Forbidden: You do not have access to that record., return to the Manage permissions section of your Greenhouse Recruiting account from step 6, update and save the corresponding permissions, and add the module again.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Greenhouse Recruiting modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nSet Up Greenhouse Recruiting Webhooks\n\nThe following Greenhouse Recruiting modules are marked with an instant tag and require you to set up webhooks before you can use them: Watch Applications, Watch Candidates, Watch Jobs, Watch Job Posts, and Watch Offers.\n\nGreenhouse Recruiting will send data to the webhook when a specific event in Greenhouse Recruiting happens.\n\nTo set up a webhook, follow these steps:\n\nAdd the corresponding instant module for the webhook type to your scenario and click Create a webhook.\n\nIn the Webhook name field, enter a name for the webhook that describes its purpose. We recommend the following format: Greenhouse Recruiting [event name] Webhook.\n\nFor example: 'Greenhouse Recruiting Watch Candidates Webhook'.\n\nSelect the corresponding connection in the Connection field. If you have not already created a connection, refer to the Connect Greenhouse Recruiting to Make section above.\n\nSelect the Event to trigger this webhook.\n\nCreate an arbitrary Secret Key of your choice in the Secret Key field. Save this key in a safe location as you will use this key when configuring the webhook in Greenhouse Recruiting. The secret key adds extra security to ensure that your Make webhook is called only by this authorized service.\n\nClick Save.\n\nCopy the generated webhook address to your clipboard and click OK.\n\nOpen your Greenhouse Recruiting account. Click on the Configure symbol > Dev Center > Web Hooks > Web Hooks.\n\nEnter the details as follows:\n\nName this web hook\n\n\t\n\nType a name that describes what the webhook does. We recommend the following format: Make - [event name].\n\nFor example: Make - Watch Candidates.\n\n\n\n\nWhen\n\n\t\n\nSelect the event for which you want to receive the triggers. The event must match the event you selected in the connection settings.\n\n\n\n\nEndpoint URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL address copied from the instant module in your scenario.\n\n\n\n\nSecret key\n\n\t\n\nEnter the secret key you defined in the instant module in your scenario.\n\n\n\n\nError recipient mail\n\n\t\n\nEnter an email address to which you want to send error reports.\n\n\n\n\nDeactivated\n\n\t\n\nSelect No.\n\nClick Create Web hook.\n\nGreenhouse Recruiting will now send data to Make through the webhook when the selected event occurs.\n\nApplication\nWatch Applications\nSearch Applications\nAdd Application to Prospect\nAdd Application to Candidate\nAdd Attachment to Application\nCandidate\nWatch Candidates\nSearch Candidates\nCreate a Prospect\nCreate a Candidate\nUpdate a Candidate\nAdd a Candidate Note\nAdd Attachment to Candidate\nJob\nWatch Jobs\nWatch Job Posts\nWatch Offers\nSearch Jobs\nSearch Job Posts\nList Approval Flows\nGet a Job\nGet a Job Post\nOther\nMake a Harvest API Call\nExample of Use - Get Offers\nGreenhouse Recruiting\nConnect Greenhouse Recruiting to Make\nSet Up Greenhouse Recruiting Webhooks\nApplication\nWatch Applications\nSearch Applications\nAdd Application to Prospect\nAdd Application to Candidate\nAdd Attachment to Application\nCandidate\nWatch Candidates\nSearch Candidates\nCreate a Prospect\nCreate a Candidate\nUpdate a Candidate\nAdd a Candidate Note\nAdd Attachment to Candidate\nJob\nWatch Jobs\nWatch Job Posts\nWatch Offers\nSearch Jobs\nSearch Job Posts\nList Approval Flows\nGet a Job\nGet a Job Post\nOther\nMake a Harvest API Call\nExample of Use - Get Offers\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

You can now edit your scenario and add more HiBob modules. Click OK.\n\nLog in to your HiBob account, and click Settings > Automation > Webhook.\n\nTo create a new webhook, click Add a new Subscriber. Enter a name and URL copied in step 1 in the URL field, and select the events you want to watch.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully set up the webhooks.\n\nHiBob\nConnect HiBob to Make\nTriggers\nWatch All Events\nActions\nMake an API Call\nGet an Employee\nComplete a Task\nSearches\nList All Employees\nList Employee's History\nLists Tasks\nSetting up HiBob webhooks\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

If you do not have one, you can create a People HR free trial account at www.peoplehr.com/trial.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting People HR to Make\n\nTo connect your People HR account to Make you need to generate an API Key in your People HR account.\n\nLog in to your People HR account.\n\nGo to Settings > API.\n\nClick the PLUS (+) button to generate a new API Key.\n\nEnter the name for the API Key and select applications you want to access using the API Key, then click Save.\n\nClick the copy icon () to copy the generated API key.\n\nGo to Make and open the People HR module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nEnter the API Key you have copied in step 5 to the respective field, enter your People HR login credentials, and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nTriggers\n\nWatch Events\n\nTriggers when an action is performed in your People HR account.\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of supported actions please refer to the People HR's Webhooks detail documentatrion.\n\nThe webhook URL needs to be generated in Make and then added to People HR API settings.\n\nAdd the Watch Events module to your Make scenario.\n\nGenerate and copy the webhook URL.\n\nLog in to your People HR account.\n\nGo to Settings > API.\n\nPaste the webhook URL you have copied in step 2 above to the Webhook URL field.\n\nNow, every time the action is performed, the Watch Events module in your Make scenario is triggered.\n\nPeople HR\nGetting Started with People HR\nConnecting People HR to Make\nTriggers\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

All Enterprise apps are currently labeled as premium tier 3 in Make.\n\nRefer to the Oracle Fusion Cloud HCM API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Oracle Fusion Cloud HCM to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must enter your Oracle Cloud service server name and login credentials. This information can be found in the Oracle Cloud service welcome email sent to your Oracle Cloud service administrator.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add an Oracle Fusion Cloud HCM module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Server Name field, enter the URL of your Oracle Cloud service. For example, servername.fa.us2.oraclecloud.com.\n\nIn the Username and Password fields, enter your Oracle Cloud service login credentials. Your account must have the necessary user permissions to be able to access the relevant records in Make.\n\nSet the connection's Scope by selecting the relevant record types.\n\nNote: If you receive a data.collection is too big error, limit the Scope selection to specific record types.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Oracle Fusion Cloud HCM modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nCaution\n\nThe connection may take up to 5 minutes to establish. You can create an account at app.deel.com/signup.\n\nRefer to the Deel API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Deel to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Deel.\n\nNote: Only the Deel API key type of connection requires obtaining the API key.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Deel\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Deel account:\n\nLog in to your Deel account.\n\nGo to the App Store section and click Developer Center.\n\nIn API access token, select which access token you want to generate: for an organization or for a person.\n\nClick Generate New Token.\n\nIn the Type a label to name your token field, enter a name for the access token. Click Next.\n\nSelect the needed scopes and click Generate. Refer to the list of modules to check which scopes you need to select.\n\nCopy the API key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Key field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Deel in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Deel module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nIn Connection type, select the type of the connection:\n\nDeel OAuth\n\nDeel API Key\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIf you chose the Deel API Key connection type, in the API Key field, enter the API key copied above.\n\nIn Environment, choose the staging that you want to connect to.\n\nOptional: Switch on the Show advanced settings toggle, enter your custom app client credentials, and select the needed scopes. For more information, refer to the Deel help documentation.\n\nIf requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/deel.\n\nNote: To create the Deel OAuth type of connection, you need to select the organizations:read scope.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Deel modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nSet Up Deel Webhooks\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nTo set up a webhook, follow these steps:\n\nAdd an Deel instant module to your scenario and click Add.\n\nOptional: Enter a name for the webhook in the Webhook name field.\n\nSelect the corresponding connection for the webhook in the Connection field.\n\nIn the Event type, select the type of the event that you want to trigger the webhook.\n\nOptional: In the Name field, enter a name for the webhook.\n\nOptional: In the Description field, enter a description for the webhook.\n\nClick Save.\n\nBuild Deel Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nRecords\n\nWith the help of these modules, you can manage records in your Deel account.\n\nWatch Records\nSearch Records\nCreate a Record\nGet a Record\nUpdate a Record\nDelete a Record\nOther\nMake an API Call\nDeel\nConnect Deel to Make\nObtain your API key in Deel\nEstablish the connection with Deel in Make\nSet Up Deel Webhooks\nBuild Deel Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

You can create an account at bamboohr.com/signup.\n\nRefer to the BambooHR API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect BambooHR to Make\n\nYou can establish two types of connections between BambooHR and Make, using your BambooHR OpenID (OAuth connection) or your BambooHR API key.\n\nEstablish a BambooHR OpenID connection\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a BambooHR module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nIn the Connection type field, select BambooHR OpenID.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Subdomain field, enter the subdomain you use to access BambooHR. For more information, refer to the BambooHR Getting Started With the API documentation. Custom apps can be created in the BambooHR developer portal.\n\nIf requested, use the following Redirect URI when creating your custom app: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/bamboohr3.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. For example, if you access BambooHR at https://mycompany.bamboohr.com, enter mycompany.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more BambooHR modules. document statuses in your Zoho Sign account.\n\nGetting Started with Zoho Sign\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Zoho Sign account\n\nIn order to use Zoho Sign with Make, it is necessary to have a Zoho Sign account. If you do not have one, you can create a Zoho Sign account at sign.zoho.eu.\n\nConnect Zoho Sign to Make\n\nTo connect your Zoho Sign account to Make follow the general instructions for Connecting to services.\n\nAfter you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Zoho Sign website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Accept button.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can now proceed with setting up the module.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nAllows you to perform a custom API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Zoho Sign account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://sign.zoho.{{connection.location}}/. E.g. /api/v1/users\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Zoho Sign API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Documents\n\nThe following API call returns documents in your Zoho Sign account:\n\nURL:\n\n/api/v1/requests\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > requests.\n\nIn our example, 2 documents were returned:\n\nZoho Sign\nGetting Started with Zoho Sign\nConnect Zoho Sign to Make\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Documents\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

projects and media and watch for new visitors in your Wistia account.\n\nTo use the Wistia modules, you must have a Wistia account. You can create an account at wistia.com.\n\nRefer to the Wistia API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Wistia to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Wistia.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Wistia\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Wistia account:\n\nLog in to your Wistia account.\n\nIn the top-right corner of the page, go to Account > Settings.\n\nIn the left sidebar, click API Access.\n\nClick New token.\n\nEnter a name for the API Token, select the relevant permissions, and click Create token.\n\nCopy the Password shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the Access Token field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Wistia in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Wistia module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Access Token field, enter the password copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Wistia modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Wistia Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nProjects\n\nWatch New Projects\n\nList Projects\n\nGet a Project\n\nCreate a Project\n\nCopy a Project\n\nUpdate a Project\n\nDelete a Project\n\nMedia\n\nWatch New Videos\n\nSearch Medias\n\nGet a Media\n\nUpload a Video\n\nCreate an Embed Code\n\nUpdate a Media\n\nDelete a Media\n\nVisitors\n\nWatch New Visitors\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nWistia\nConnect Wistia to Make\nObtain your API key in Wistia\nEstablish the connection with Wistia in Make\nBuild Wistia Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document Managementeversign\neversign\n\nThe eversign modules enable you to monitor, list, retrieve, download, create, cancel, and delete documents and templates in your eversign account.\n\nGetting Started with eversign\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAn eversign account\n\nIn order to use eversign with Make, it is necessary to have an eversign account. If you do not have one, you can create an eversign account at eversign.com/signup.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting eversign to Make\n\nTo connect your eversign account to Make you need to obtain your API Key.\n\n1. Log in to your eversign account.\n\n2. Click on your profile icon in the top-left corner and select the Developer option from the menu.\n\n3. Copy the provided API Access Key.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the eversign module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. Enter the API Key you have copied in step 3 to the respective field and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nDocuments\nWatch New Documents\n\nRetrieves document details when a document requires your action, is waiting for others, is completed, cancelled or draft has been created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to monitor documents for.\n\n\n\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the document's status to filter your results by.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of documents Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nList Documents\n\nRetrieves a list of documents in your account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to retrieve documents for.\n\n\n\n\nType\n\n\t\n\nSelect the document's status to filter your results by.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of documents Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet a Document\n\nRetrieves document details.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to retrieve the document for.\n\n\n\n\nDocument ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the document you want to retrieve details about.\n\nDownload a Final Document\n\nDownloads a final PDF version of a document.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to download the documents for.\n\n\n\n\nDocument ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the document you want to download.\n\nDownload an Original Document\n\nDownloads an original PDF version of a document.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to download the document for.\n\n\n\n\nDocument ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the document you want to download.\n\nCreate a Document\n\nCreates a new document.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to create the document for.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter a document title.\n\n\n\n\nMessage\n\n\t\n\nEnter a document message.\n\n\n\n\nFiles\n\n\t\n\nAdd the document files you want to upload or add (existing file) to the document.\n\nFile name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the file you want to upload.\n\n\n\n\nSpecify file by\n\n\t\n\nSelect how you want to provide the file.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the ID of the file that has been already uploaded to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nFile URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL of the file you want to upload.\n\n\n\n\nFile upload\n\n\t\n\nMap the file data from the previous module or enter the data manually.\n\n\n\n\nFields\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the fields that should be placed on the document.\n\n(reference: https://eversign.com/api/documentation/methods#create-document)\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nDescription\n\n\n\n\ntype\n\n\t\n\nThe type of field to be placed. You can view a list of all available field types by clicking here.\n\n\n\n\nx\n\n\t\n\nThe field's horizontal margin from the left side of the document in pixels.\n\n\n\n\ny\n\n\t\n\nThe field's vertical margin from the top of the document in pixels.\n\n\n\n\nwidth\n\n\t\n\nThe field's width in pixels.\n\n\n\n\nheight\n\n\t\n\nThe field's height in pixels.\n\n\n\n\npage\n\n\t\n\nThe number of the document page where the field should be placed.\n\n\n\n\nsigner\n\n\t\n\nThe unique ID of the signer this field should be assigned to. If this field should become a No Signer field, please set this parameter to OWNER.\n\n\n\n\nname\n\n\t\n\nThe field's field label.\n\n\n\n\nidentifier\n\n\t\n\nThe field's field identifier.\n\n\n\n\nrequired\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 in order to make this field a required field.\n\n\n\n\nreadonly\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 in order to make this field a read-only field.\n\n\n\n\nvalidation_type\n\n\t\n\nEnable field validation for this field. Available validation types are email_address, letters_only and numbers_only.\n\n\n\n\ntext_style\n\n\t\n\nThe letters B for bold, U for underlined and I for italic, in the order of your choice. Example: BUI\n\n\n\n\ntext_font\n\n\t\n\nSet the font identifier to your preferred font, e.g. arial. Jump to section field style to learn about supported fonts.\n\n\n\n\ntext_size\n\n\t\n\nSet to your preferred font size number (string or integer), e.g. 16.\n\n\n\n\ntext_color\n\n\t\n\nSet to your preferred HEX color code, e.g. #FF0000\n\n\n\n\nvalue\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 to mark checkbox or radio fields checked; or specify text content for note or text fields. For dropdown fields, set this parameter to an option value in order to pre-select it.\n\n\n\n\noptions\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter must contain a simple JSON array containing all available options of a dropdown field. In order to pre-select an option, simply set the value parameter to the option value.\n\n\n\n\ngroup\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to identify radio button groups. radio fields belonging to the same group must carry the same group parameter. Please note that this parameter must be numeric.\n\n\n\n\nSigners\n\n\t\n\nAdd signers of the document.\n\n(reference: https://eversign.com/api/documentation/methods#create-document)\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nDescription\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to specify the full name of the current signer.\n\n\n\n\nEmail\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to specify the email address of the current signer.\n\n\n\n\nSigner ID\n\n\t\n\nA unique identification number (integer) for this signer. We recommend numbering your signers from 1 to X.\n\n\n\n\nOrder\n\n\t\n\nIf the use_signer_order parameter is set to 1, set this parameter to the signer order number of the current signer.\n\n\n\n\nPIN\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to specify a signer PIN for the current signer.\n\n\n\n\nMessage\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter can be used to specify a custom message (upon document delivery) for the current signer. Please note that for the current signer the general document message will be overridden by this parameter.\n\n\n\n\nDeliver email\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is only applicable if embedded_signing_enabled is set to 1. By default, signers of embedded documents are not notified (default: deliver_email: 0) about a new document to be signed. Set deliver_email to 1 to send a notification email to this signer anyway.\n\n\n\n\nLanguage\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to specify the language in which signing notifications (emails), the document status page and the signature process will appear for this signer.\n\nCancel a Document\n\nCancels a document.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to cancel the document for.\n\n\n\n\nDocument ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the document you want to cancel.\n\nDelete a Document\n\nDeletes a document.\n\nOnly cancelled documents and draft documents or templates can be deleted.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nBusiness\n\n\t\n\nSelect the business you want to delete the document for.\n\n\n\n\nDocument ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the document you want to delete.\n\nTemplates\nWatch New Templates\n\nRetrieves template details when a template in the specified status is created.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eversign https://eversign.com/api/documentation/methods#create-document)\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nDescription\n\n\n\n\ntype\n\n\t\n\nThe type of field to be placed. You can view a list of all available field types by clicking here.\n\n\n\n\nx\n\n\t\n\nThe field's horizontal margin from the left side of the document in pixels.\n\n\n\n\ny\n\n\t\n\nThe field's vertical margin from the top of the document in pixels.\n\n\n\n\nwidth\n\n\t\n\nThe field's width in pixels.\n\n\n\n\nheight\n\n\t\n\nThe field's height in pixels.\n\n\n\n\npage\n\n\t\n\nThe number of the document page where the field should be placed.\n\n\n\n\nsigner\n\n\t\n\nThe unique ID of the signer this field should be assigned to. If this field should become a No Signer field, please set this parameter to OWNER.\n\n\n\n\nname\n\n\t\n\nThe field's field label.\n\n\n\n\nidentifier\n\n\t\n\nThe field's field identifier.\n\n\n\n\nrequired\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 in order to make this field a required field.\n\n\n\n\nreadonly\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 in order to make this field a read-only field.\n\n\n\n\nvalidation_type\n\n\t\n\nEnable field validation for this field. Available validation types are email_address, letters_only and numbers_only.\n\n\n\n\ntext_style\n\n\t\n\nThe letters B for bold, U for underlined and I for italic, in an order of your choice. Example: BUI\n\n\n\n\ntext_font\n\n\t\n\nSet the font identifier to your preferred font, e.g. arial. Jump to section field style to learn about supported fonts.\n\n\n\n\ntext_size\n\n\t\n\nSet to your preferred font size number (string or integer), e.g. 16.\n\n\n\n\ntext_color\n\n\t\n\nSet to your preferred HEX color code, e.g. #FF0000\n\n\n\n\nvalue\n\n\t\n\nSet to 1 to mark checkbox or radio fields checked; or specify text content for note or text fields. For dropdown fields, set this parameter to an option value in order to pre-select it.\n\n\n\n\noptions\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter must contain a simple JSON array containing all available options of a dropdown field. In order to pre-select an option, simply set the value parameter to the option value.\n\n\n\n\ngroup\n\n\t\n\nThis parameter is used to identify radio button groups. radio fields belonging to the same group must carry the same group parameter. Please note that this parameter must be numeric.\n\n\n\n\nFile name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the file you want to upload.\n\n\n\n\nSpecify file by\n\n\t\n\nSelect how you want to provide the file.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the ID of the file that has been already uploaded to your eversign account.\n\n\n\n\nFile URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL of the file you want to upload.\n\n\n\n\nFile upload\n\n\t\n\nMap the file data from the previous module or enter the data manually.\n\n\n\n\nFields\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the fields that should be placed on the document.\n\n(reference: https://eversign.com/api/documentation/methods#create-document)\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nDescription\n\n\n\n\ntype\n\n\t\n\nThe type of field to be placed. Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementeSignatures.io\neSignatures.io\n\nFrom creating contracts to keeping track of the signed ones, the eSignatures.io modules enable you to easily automate your contract sending process from start to finish.\n\nGetting Started with eSignatures.io\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAn eSignatures.io account\n\nIn order to use eSignatures.io with Make, it is necessary to have an eSignatures.io account. If you do not have one, you can create an eSignatures.io account at esignatures.io.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting eSignatures.io to Make\n\nTo connect your eSignatures.io account to Make you need to obtain the Secret Token from your eSignatures.io account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your eSignatures.io account.\n\n2. Go to API settings in the top-right corner.\n\n3. Copy the Secret Token to your clipboard.\n\n4. Go to Make and open the eSignatures.io module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n5. In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\n6. In the Secret Token field, enter the token details copied in step 3, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nTriggers\n\nAll triggers need a webhook in order for them to function. In your eSignatures.io module, choose any of the triggers then generate a webhook. This will automatically connect the webhook from Make to your eSignatures.io account.\n\nTrigger Options\n\n\t\n\nDescription\n\n\n\n\nWatch Contract Sent To Signer\n\n\t\n\nTriggered when the contract is sent to a signer.\n\n\n\n\nWatch Contract Signed\n\n\t\n\nTriggered when all signers have signed the contract.\n\n\n\n\nWatch Contract Signed By A Signer\n\n\t\n\nTriggered when each individual signer has signed the contract.\n\n\n\n\nWatch Webhook Error Notifications\n\n\t\n\nTriggered when an error has occurred (eg. delivery issue).\n\nActions\nCreate a Contract\n\nCreates a new contract.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your eSignatures.io account.\n\n\t\n\n\nTest Mode\n\n\t\n\nChoose between sending a Live contract or a Test contract.\n\n\t\n\n\nTemplate\n\n\t\n\nSelect the template you want to use for the contract.\n\n\t\n\n\nPlaceholder\n\nfields\n\n\t\n\nSpecify Placeholders in the template to be replaced with your custom data.\n\n\t\n\n\nSigners\n\n\t\n\nAPI key\n\n\t\n\nthis is a Placeholder name as specified in the template editor.\n\n\n\t\n\nValue\n\n\t\n\ndata that would replace the Placeholder.\n\n\n\t\n\nAdd and specify signers of the contract.\n\n\t\n\t\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nname of the signer.\n\n\n\t\n\nEmail\n\n\t\n\nemail address of the signer (for identification).\n\n\n\t\n\nMobile\n\n\t\n\nmobile number of the signer (for identification).\n\n\n\t\n\nTicking the box beside Show advanced settings in the Signer field allows you to add.\n\n\t\n\t\n\nCompany Name\n\n\t\n\ncompany name of the signer.\n\n\n\t\n\nRedirect URL\n\n\t\n\nthe URL that the signer will be redirected to after signing the. contract.\n\n\n\t\n\nAuto Sign\n\n\t\n\nenable this option to automatically add the signer's signature to the contract.\n\n\n\t\n\nSigning Order\n\n\t\n\nto specify the order of signers. When the same number is used for two or more signers, they will receive the signature request at the same time.\n\n\n\n\n(Advanced settings) Contract Title\n\n\t\n\nEnter the unique title of the contract (the template name is used when not specified). It appears in emails, generated documents, and dashboard pages.\n\n\t\n\n\n(Advanced settings) Metadata\n\n\t\n\nAdd your own custom information (eg. your own record ID).\n\n\t\n\n\n(Advanced settings) Language\n\n\t\n\nSelect the signer page/email language.\n\n\t\neSignatures.io\nGetting Started with eSignatures.io\nConnecting eSignatures.io to Make\nTriggers\nActions\nCreate a Contract\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

For more information, see the documentation.\n\nAbout the Chained Document (in Signers)\n\nThe easiest way of working with the chained document is by sending the requests backward. Please see the following example:\n\nContext: You want to send three different documents to a customer.\n\n1. Create three documents using the Create a Document module.\n\n2. Create a SignRequest using the Create a SignRequest module with Document 3 URL address in the documents field and Document 2 URL address in the after_documents field in the signers' array. This will not trigger a SignRequest email to be sent to the signer.\n\n3. You create a SignRequest using the Create a SignRequest module with Document 2 URL address in documents field and Document 1 URL address in the after_documents field in the signers' array. This will not trigger a SignRequest email to be sent to the signer.\n\n4. You create a SignRequest using the Create a SignRequest module with Document 1 URL address in the documents field without providing any details in the after_documents field. Because this SignRequest has no after_documents email, it triggers a SignRequest email to be sent to the signer.\n\nNote\n\nResending the SignRequest email (in this case for Document 3 and Document 2) will trigger the SignRequest email to be sent to the signer even though there was none sent before.\n\nWhen after_document references a document where the signer in question already has signed or declined they will still receive a SignRequest email as we cannot redirect them anymore. It's only possible to reference documents that are not fully signed (or declined) yet.\n\n\n\n\nEmail Sender\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the sender's email address. Required when authenticated as a Team. The reply-to email address\n\n\n\n\nEmail Sender Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the sender's name who is sending the SignRequest.\n\n\n\n\nEmail Subject\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the email subject including from templates, and make API calls.\n\nTo get started with Synthesia, create an account at synthesia.io. You must have a paid Synthesia account to use the Synthesia API and establish a connection to Make. Refer to Synthesia Pricing for information regarding accounts, usage limits, and features.\n\nRefer to the Synthesia API documentation for the list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Synthesia to Make\n\nTo connect Synthesia to Make, you must first obtain an API key from your Synthesia account.\n\nLog in to your Synthesia account.\n\nIf you have multiple Workspaces in your account, select the relevant Workspace in the top left corner.\n\nIn the top right corner, click on your Profile icon > Integrations.\n\nTo use an existing API key, go to Step 5. To create a new API key, click Add.\n\nNext to your API key, click ... > Copy.\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Synthesia module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter your API key copied in Step 5.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Synthesia modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Synthesia Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTriggers\n\nWatch a Video Completed\n\nActions\n\nCreate a Video from a Template\n\nCreate a Video\n\nMake an API Call\n\nSynthesia\nConnect Synthesia to Make\nBuild Synthesia Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Translation modules allow you to create translations in your Simpleen Translation account.\n\nGetting Started with Simpleen Translation\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Simpleen Translation account\n\nIn order to use Simpleen Translation with Make, it is necessary to have a Simpleen Translation account. For example: /glossaries\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Simpleen Translation API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Languages\n\nThe following API call returns all the languages from your Simpleen Translation account:\n\nURL:\n\n/languages\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body.\n\nIn our example, 16 languages were returned:\n\nSimpleen Translation\nGetting Started with Simpleen Translation\nConnect Simpleen Translation to Make\nActions\nCreate a Translation\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Languages\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

and monitor the contacts, envelopes, partners, users, and templates in your Signable account.\n\nTo use the Signable modules, you must have a Signable account. You can create an account at signable.co.uk.\n\nRefer to the Signable API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Signable to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nObtain your API key in Signable.\n\nEstablish the connection in Make.\n\nObtain your API key in Signable\n\nTo obtain your API key from your Signable account:\n\nLog in to your Signable account.\n\nIn the top right corner, click on your Profile icon > Company Settings.\n\nClick API & Webhooks.\n\nIn the API Keys section, click + Add API Key.\n\nEnter a name, and click Save.\n\nClick Show key.\n\nCopy the Key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Key field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Signable in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Signable module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Signable modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Signable Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nContacts\n\nWatch Contact Created\n\nCreate a Contact\n\nUpdate a Contact\n\nGet a Contact\n\nList Contacts\n\nDelete a Contact\n\nEnvelopes\n\nWatch Envelope Signed\n\nWatch Envelope Opened\n\nWatch Envelope Completed\n\nWatch Envelope Created\n\nWatch Envelope Rejected\n\nWatch Envelope Cancelled\n\nCreate an Envelope from Template\n\nCreate an Envelope\n\nSend a Reminder for an Envelope\n\nCancel an Envelope\n\nGet an Envelope\n\nDelete an Envelope\n\nPartners\n\nCreate a Partner\n\nUpdate a Partner\n\nGet a Partner\n\nList Partners\n\nDelete a Partner\n\nUsers\n\nWatch User Created\n\nCreate a User\n\nUpdate a User\n\nGet a User\n\nList Users\n\nDelete a User\n\nTemplates\n\nWatch Template Created\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nNote\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. the scenario from your iPhone or iPad and send the desired data to Make.\n\nGetting Started With Shortcuts\n\nPrerequisites\n\niPhone or iPad with iOS 12 (or higher)\n\nShortcuts app\n\nConnect Shortcuts to Make\n\nTo connect Shortcuts to Make, you need to generate a webhook URL in Make and then insert the generated webhook URL to the Shortcuts app installed on your iOS device. To do so, follow the steps below:\n\nStep 1: Download and install Shortcuts from App Store.\n\nStep 2: Select an action you want to send data from.\n\nStep 3: Add the Watch Shortcuts module to the scenario, and generate the webhook URL.\n\nStep 4: Insert the webhook URL to Shortcuts.\n\nStep 5: Specify the payload that will be sent to your Make scenario.\n\nStep 6: Test your Shortcuts app integration.\n\nStep 1: Download and Install Shortcuts From App Store\n\nFrom your iPhone or iPad, navigate to https://apps.apple.com/us/app/shortcuts/id915249334, and install the Shortcuts app.\n\nStep 2: Select an Action You Want To Send Data From\n\nOpen the Shortcuts app () you have installed in step 1 above.\n\nTap the +Create Shortcut tile.\n\nAdd the action you want to send data to your scenario from.\n\nNote\n\nYou can skip this step if you just want to trigger your scenario without any data being sent.\n\nHere are some examples of actions you can use to send data to the Make scenario:\n\nNote\n\nWe will use the Get Current Weather action as an example, but you can choose one or more other actions.\n\nGet Current Weather - to send the current weather to your Make scenario.\n\nGet Current Location - to send the device's address to your Make scenario.\n\nDictate Text - to trigger the Make scenario with your voice and send the speech converted to text to the scenario.\n\nAsk for Input - to trigger the scenario and send the text, number, URL, or date you enter on your iOS device to your Make scenario.\n\nGet Latest Photos - to send information about the latest photo on your device.\n\nContacts - to send the selected contact to your Make scenario.\n\nGet Clipboard - to send the content of your clipboard to the Make scenario.\n\nStep 3: Add the Shortcuts Module to the Scenario and Generate the Webhook URL\n\nAdd the Watch Shortcuts module to your Make scenario.\n\nGenerate and copy the webhook URL.\n\nStep 4: Insert the Webhook URL to Shortcuts\n\nAdd the URL action to the Shortcut.\n\nPaste the webhook URL you have generated in Step 3 above.\n\nNote\n\nIf both of your devices are Apple devices, we recommend you use the Universal Clipboard feature to copy-paste the webhook URL. Otherwise, you can send the webhook URL by email to yourself or use third-party services (such as justpaste.it, pastebin.com, or privatebin.net).\n\nStep 5: Specify the Payload That Will Be Sent to Your Make Scenario\n\nAdd the Get Contents of URL action to the Shortcut.\n\nTap to open the Get Contents of URL action's Advanced settings, and set it as follows:\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nPOST\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nNo headers required.\n\n\n\n\nRequest Body\n\n\t\n\nJSON\n\n\n\n\nAdd new field\n\n\t\n\nTap Add new field, and select the Text value type.\n\nEnter the desired name to the Key field, and tap, for example, the Weather Conditions () in order to insert it into the Value field (or select another property you want to send to Make).Add more fields if needed.Tap Done.\n\nStep 6: Test Your Shortcuts Integration\n\nTo test if the data from your iOS device is received correctly, go to your scenario, and run the Watch Shortcuts module only using the Run this module only function.\n\nOpen the Shortcuts app on your iPhone or iPad, and tap the tile of the Shortcut to run actions you have defined in the steps above.\n\nThe Watch Shortcuts module in your scenario is triggered and receives the data from the Shortcut.\n\nYou can now connect other modules to build your Make scenario.\n\nShortcuts\nGetting Started With Shortcuts\nConnect Shortcuts to Make\nStep 1: Download and Install Shortcuts From App Store\nStep 2: Select an Action You Want To Send Data From\nStep 3: Add the Shortcuts Module to the Scenario and Generate the Webhook URL\nStep 4: Insert the Webhook URL to Shortcuts\nStep 5: Specify the Payload That Will Be Sent to Your Make Scenario\nStep 6: Test Your Shortcuts Integration\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

folders, and file permissions on a remote server.\n\nTo use SFTP modules, you must have an SFTP account on some hosting.\n\nEstablish the connection with SFTP in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a SFTP module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Host field, enter the host address of the server you want to connect.\n\nIn the Post field, enter the SFTP server port. It must be a number between 1 and 65535. The default value is 22.\n\nIn the Auth type dropdown list, select the authorization method you want to use for connecting to the SFTP server.\n\nIn the User name field, enter the user name that you use to enter the server.\n\nOnly for the User name and password auth type: In the Password field, enter the password that you use to enter the server.\n\nOnly for the User name and key auth type: In the Private key field, upload the private key to use the client-side authorization.\n\nNote\n\nUpload your certificate (P12, PFX, or PEM file) to use TLS using your self-signed certificate. If you use the client-side certificate authorization, you can enter your CA certificate here. Refer to our Help Center for more information.\n\nOptional: Set up an algorithm.\n\nImportant\n\nThe blowfish-cbc cipher option stopped functioning since March 19, 2024.\n\nClick Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more SFTP modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild SFTP Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTriggers\n\nWatch files in a folder\n\nWatch subfolders in a folder\n\nActions\n\nList a folder's content\n\nGet files\n\nGet a file\n\nUpload a file\n\nRename a file\n\nMove a file\n\nDelete a file\n\nUpdate file permissions\n\nNote: Use the chmod parameters, for example, 777 or -rwxrwxrwx. insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your Revv Document account.\n\nClick Settings > Revv API > Add OAuth application. For example, if your account's URL address is https:xyz.revv.so then your subdomain is xyz.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the details copied in step 4.\n\nConfirm the access by clicking Authorize.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nDocuments\nNote\n\nYou do not have to add the webhooks in the Revv Documents as it is automatically done for you once you add and save an instant trigger module to your scenario.\n\nWath Document Stage Changed\nWatch Document Signed by All Signers\nList Documents\nSearch Document Activities\nGet a Document\nCreate a Document\nSend a Document for eSignature\nSend a Document to Fill and eSign\nSave Document Signatory Details\nUpdate Document Signatories\nClone a Document\nFolders\nList Folders\nCreate a Folder\nMove Folders\nDelete Folders\nContacts\nList Contacts\nCreate a Contact\nGet a Contact\nUpdate a Contact\nDelete a Contact\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Folders\nRevv Documents\nGetting Started with Revv Documents\nConnect Revv Documents to Make\nDocuments\nWath Document Stage Changed\nWatch Document Signed by All Signers\nList Documents\nSearch Document Activities\nGet a Document\nCreate a Document\nSend a Document for eSignature\nSend a Document to Fill and eSign\nSave Document Signatory Details\nUpdate Document Signatories\nClone a Document\nFolders\nList Folders\nCreate a Folder\nMove Folders\nDelete Folders\nContacts\nList Contacts\nCreate a Contact\nGet a Contact\nUpdate a Contact\nDelete a Contact\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Folders\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

retrieve, or generate documents in your PDFMonkey account.\n\nGetting Started with PDFMonkey\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA PDFMonkey account\n\nIn order to use PDFMonkey with Make, it is necessary to have a PDFMonkey account. If you do not have one, you can create a PDFMonkey account at PDFMonkey.\n\nConnect PDFMonkey to Make\n\nTo connect your PDFMonkey account to Make, obtain the API Secret Key from your PDFMonkey account.\n\nLog in to your PDFMonkey account.\n\nClick your email address in the top-right corner and select the My Account option from the menu.\n\nClick the Show my secret key link to display your API Secret Key. Copy the provided API Secret Key.\n\nGo to Make and open the PDFMonkey module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nEnter the API Secret Key you have copied in step 3 to the respective field and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nThe connection has been established. You can proceed with setting up the module.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nAllows you to perform a custom API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your PDFMonkey account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.pdfmonkey.io/api/v1.For example: /documents.\n\nNote\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the PDFMonkey API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET\n\nto retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST\n\nto create a new entry.\n\nPUT\n\nto update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH\n\nto make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE\n\nto delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery string\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Documents\n\nThe following API call returns all documents in your PDFMonkey account:\n\nURL:\n\n/documents\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nThe result can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > documents.\n\nIn our example, 2 documents were returned:\n\nPDFMonkey\nGetting Started with PDFMonkey\nConnect PDFMonkey to Make\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Documents\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

If you do not have one, you can create a Nusii account at nusii.com/pricing/.\n\nNote\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnect Nusii to Make\n\nTo connect your Nusii account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your Nusii account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\nLog in to your Nusii account and open your Dashboard.\n\nClick Settings > Integrations & API > here. Copy the API Token to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the Nusii module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API token copied in step 2, and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nClients\nWatch Client Created\nList Clients\nGet a Client\nCreate a Client\nUpdate a Client\nDelete a Client\nProposals\nWatch Proposal Created\nWatch Proposal Updated\nWatch Proposal Sent\nWatch Proposal Accepted\nWatch Proposal Rejected\nList Proposals\nGet a Proposal\nCreate a Proposal\nSend a Proposal\nDelete a Proposal\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Users\nNusii\nGetting Started with Nusii\nConnect Nusii to Make\nClients\nWatch Client Created\nList Clients\nGet a Client\nCreate a Client\nUpdate a Client\nDelete a Client\nProposals\nWatch Proposal Created\nWatch Proposal Updated\nWatch Proposal Sent\nWatch Proposal Accepted\nWatch Proposal Rejected\nList Proposals\nGet a Proposal\nCreate a Proposal\nSend a Proposal\nDelete a Proposal\nOther\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Users\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Notebook\nZoho Sign\nZoho Writer\nHR management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementMicrosoft Word Templates\nMicrosoft Word Templates\nGetting started with Microsoft Word Templates\n\nMicrosoft Word Templates enables you to merge data provided by various services with templates and produce Microsoft Word documents as a result.\n\nTemplate:\n\nCreated document:\n\nTemplate creation\n\nA Template is a regular Microsoft Word document (.docx file) with special tags in its text that determine where and how to merge/fill in data. There are three types of tags: Simple value, Condition and Loop or section.\n\nSimple value\n\nA Simple value tag is simply replaced with a corresponding value. The tag's name corresponds to the Key field's value, which is placed inside double curly braces: e.g. {{name}}.\n\nNote\n\nThe Microsoft Word Templates app accepts only single-line plain text for replacement values. When adding line breaks, they will be viewed as spaces and won't affect the formatting of the text.\n\nTemplate:\n\n> Hi {{name}}!\n\n\nModule's setup:\n\nCreated document:\n\n> Hi Petr!\n\nCondition\n\nA Condition tag enables you to wrap certain parts of a text that should be rendered conditionally. To wrap the conditional text, place it between the opening and closing tags. The name of the opening tag is prepended with a hash sign #, the name of the closing tag is prepended with a slash /.\n\nTemplate:\n\n> {{#hasPhone}}Phone: {{phone}} {{/hasPhone}}\n> {{#hasEmail}}Email: {{email}} {{/hasEmail}}\n\n\nModule's setup:\n\nCreated document:\n\n > Phone: 123456\nLoop or section\n\nA Loop or section tag enables you to repeat parts of a text. Similarly to the Condition tag, to wrap the repeated text, place it between the opening and closing tags. The name of the opening tag is prepended with a hash sign #, the name of the closing tag is prepended with a slash /.\n\nWhen using loops, you can choose to employ either the Fill out a document module or the Fill a document with a batch of data aggregator module.\n\nFill out a document\n\nIf you employ Fill out a document module, the content of the field Value has to be an array of collections, where:\n\nEach collection corresponds to one data entry and contains one item entry\n\nItem entry contains a collection with two items key and value\n\nItem key contains the tag's name\n\nitem value contains the tag's value\n\nTemplate:\n\n> {{#contact}}\n>     {{name}}, {{phone}}\n> {{/contact}}\n               \n\nModule's setup:\n\nCreated document:\n\n> Jan Toman, 1234\n> Eduard Salo, 7899999\n               \n\nYou can also execute a loop to populate a table. The example below shows how to create such table in a template:\n\nFill a document with a batch of data\n\nIf your data entries come as separate bundles, you may prefer to employ the Fill a document with a batch of data aggregator module. You can employ this module also if your data entries come as an array - just employ the iterator module to transform the content of the array into a series of bundles.\n\nThe main advantage of the Fill a document with a batch of data module is that it enables you to easily setup the structure required for the Value field and map items to each value item. In contrast to the Fill out a document module, the field Values contains only a single entry, the actual entries will be created and populated for each incoming bundle. The template will be produced after all input bundles have been processed. The aggregator module is useful, especially when creating lists or reports.\n\nExample: Export Google Contacts into a table\n\nThe first module loads the template. The next module retrieves all contacts from the specified group in Google Contacts. The aggregator module then aggregates all values retrieved from Google Contacts and merges them into the template. Finally, the last module will save the filled template to a desired location.\n\nTemplate:\n\nModule's setup:\n\nCreated document:\n\nMicrosoft Word Templates\nGetting started with Microsoft Word Templates\nTemplate creation\nSimple value\nCondition\nLoop or section\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementKlippa\nKlippa\n\nKlippa modules allow you to automate document management, classification, and data extraction from your Klippa account.\n\nGetting Started with Klippa\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Klippa account - create an account at klippa.com\n\nConnect Klippa to Make\n\nTo connect your Klippa to Make you need to obtain an API key by contacting the Klippa team at Klippa Support team and inserting it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your Make account and add a module from the AX Semantics app into an Make scenario.\n\n2. Click Add next to the Connection field.\n\n3. In the Connection name, enter a name for the connection.\n\n4. In the API Key field, enter the API key received from the Klippa support team and click Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nActions\nParse a Document\n\nParse a document in the Klippa system and return all information in JSON.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Klippa account.\n\n\n\n\nDocument Source\n\n\t\n\nSelect the source of the document:\n\nDocument URL Address\n\nMap Document File\n\n\n\n\nDocument URL\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the document URL address which you want to parse.\n\n\n\n\nSource File\n\n\t\n\nAdd the file details:\n\nFilename: Enter (map) the document name.\n\nData: Enter (map) the document data.\n\n\n\n\nTemplate\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the template to use for parsing the document.\n\n\n\n\nPDF Text Extraction\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the option to extract the PDF text. For example, full, fast.\n\n\n\n\nUser Data\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the user metadata in JSON format to give to the parser. This field only works with templates that are configured to accept user data.\n\n\n\n\nUser Data Set External ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the User Data Set External ID.\n\n\n\n\nHash Duplicate Group ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) an identifier to use when saving or detecting hash duplicates. It helps you to allow to have the same document scanned more than once for multiple groups. When doing a scan, the combination of the Hash Group ID and the document hash are used to detect the duplicates. This value is saved hashed on Klippa's side. The common use cases are Company ID, Campaign ID, and User ID.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Klippa account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://custom-ocr.klippa.com/api For example: /v1/parseDocument\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the Klippa API Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST to create a new entry.\n\nPUT to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH to make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE to delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - Get API Usage Statistics\n\nThe following API call returns API usage statistics from your Klippa account:\n\nURL: /v1/statistics\n\nMethod: GET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > data. In our example, 1 record is returned:\n\nAdvanced Settings\n\nThese settings can be used if you want to modify the parser more.\n\nTemplate\n\nSelect a template for the parser to identify what kind of document it would be. It can be that when changing the template settings, the output data is different.\n\nPDF Text Extraction\n\nUse full when you want the best quality scan, use fast when you want fast scan results. Fast will try to extract the text from the PDF. Full actually scans the full PDF which is slower.\n\nUser Data\n\nThe User Data allows for sending additional data into the parser and can be used to enable extra features, improve the recognition of certain fields and improve the processing speed. All fields are optional, documents may be submitted without this field. For more information, refer to the Klippa API documentation.\n\nUser Dataset External ID\n\nThis option is only available when you have custom Datasets and the API has access to these datasets, For more information, contact the Klippa support team.\n\nThe ID of the dataset in your own system, The system returns this id in the merchant_id field if there is a match.\n\nHash Duplicate Group ID\n\nAn identifier to use when saving or detecting hash duplicates. This way you can allow to have the same document scanned more than once for multiple groups. When doing a scan, the combination of the Hash Group ID and the document Hash will be used to detect duplicates. This value is saved hashed on the side of Klippa. The common use cases are Company ID, Campaign ID, and User ID.\n\nKlippa\nConnect Klippa to Make\nActions\nParse a Document\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - Get API Usage Statistics\nAdvanced Settings\nTemplate\nPDF Text Extraction\nUser Data\nUser Dataset External ID\nHash Duplicate Group ID\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

E.g. Oxanium\n\nSee also the documentation on the HTML/CSS to Image website.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nAllows you to perform a custom API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your HTML/CSS to Image account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://hcti.io/v1. Dropbox Sign.\n\nWith the Dropbox Sign modules in Make, you can:\n\nsend, retrieve, cancel, and list the signature requests and templates\n\ncreate, retrieve, list, and delete the templates\n\ndelete your teams\n\nwatch events\n\ncall APIs\n\nTo get started with Dropbox Sign, create an account at dropboxsign.com.\n\nFor the list of endpoints, refer to the Dropox Sign API documentation.\n\nConnect Dropbox Sign to Make\n\nTo connect the Dropbox Sign app with the Make:\n\nLog in to your Make and add a module from the Dropbox Sign into a Make scenario.\n\nClick Add next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection and click Save.\n\nIf prompted, log in to your Dropbox Sign account and click Accept to authorize Make to access your Dropbox Sign account.\n\nYou have successfully connected the Dropbox Sign app with Make and can now build scenarios.\n\nBuild Dropbox Sign Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nSend a Signature Request\n\nCreates and sends a new signature request with the submitted documents.\n\nSend a Signature Request with a Template\n\nCreates and sends a new signature request based on a template.\n\nCancel an Incomplete Signature Request\n\nCancels an incomplete signature request. This action is not reversible.\n\nSends a Request Reminder\n\nSends an email to the signer reminding them to sign the signature request.\n\nGet a Signature Request\n\nRetrieves a signature request.\n\nList Signature Requests\n\nRetrieves all signature requests (both inbound and outbound) you have access to.\n\nGet Signature Request Files\n\nRetrieves a copy of the documents belonging to a signature request.\n\nCreate a Template Using an Existing Template\n\nCreates a new template using the overlay of an existing template.\n\nGet a Template\n\nRetrieves a template.\n\nList Templates\n\nRetrieves the list of templates that are accessible to you.\n\nGet Template Files\n\nRetrieves a copy of a template's original files.\n\nDelete a Template\n\nDeletes the specified template.\n\nDelete your Team\n\nDeletes your team.\n\nWatch Events\n\nWatch all events involving your account.\n\nMake an API Call\n\nPerforms an arbitrary authorized API call.\n\nDropbox Sign\nConnect Dropbox Sign to Make\nBuild Dropbox Sign Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Suite account\n\nIn order to use Google Team Drive with Make, it is necessary to have a G Suite account. If you do not have one, you can create a G Suite account at gsuite.google.com/signup/basic/welcome.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting Google Team Drive to Make\n\nTo connect your Google Team Drive account to Make follow the general instructions for Connecting to services.\n\nAfter you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Google website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Allow button.\n\nTriggers\nWatch Files\n\nReturns file details when a new file is added and/or modified in the specified folder.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nTeam Drive\n\n\t\n\nSelect the shared drive you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the folder within the shared drive.\n\n\n\n\nWhat files to watch\n\n\t\n\nSelect the type of files you want to watch.\n\n\n\n\nConvert Google Documents files to format\n\n\t\n\nSelect the format you want the watched files converted to.\n\n\n\n\nWatch\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to monitor the folder for new and modified files or just for new files.\n\n\n\n\nMaximum number of downloaded files\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of files Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nActions\nUpload a File\n\nUploads a file to the specified shared drive.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nTeam Drive\n\n\t\n\nSelect the shared drive you want to upload a file to.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the folder within the shared drive.\n\n\n\n\nSource File\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the file you want to upload to the shared drive.\n\nMap the file you want to upload from the previous module (e.g. HTTP > Get a File or Dropbox > Get a file), or enter the file name and file data manually.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title of the file that will be displayed in the shared folder.\n\n\n\n\nConvert a File\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to convert the file to the corresponding Google format in your shared folder.\n\nUpdate a File\n\nAllows you to change the file name and/or file content.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nTeam Drive\n\n\t\n\nSelect the shared drive that contains the file you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the folder within the shared drive.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the file you want to update.\n\n\n\n\nSource File\n\n\t\n\nSpecify the new file name and new file data.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter the new title for the updated file.\n\n\n\n\nConvert a File\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to convert the file to the corresponding Google format in your shared folder.\n\nCopy a File\n\nCopies a specified file to the selected folder.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nTeam Drive\n\n\t\n\nSelect the shared drive that contains the file you want to copy.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the target folder you want to copy the file to.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the file you want to copy.\n\n\n\n\nThe name of the copy file\n\n\t\n\nEnter the new file name if you want it to be changed in the target location.\n\nDelete a File\n\nDeletes a specified file.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter or map the ID of the file you want to delete.\n\nMove a File to the trash bin.\n\nGet a File\n\nRetrieves details about the specified file.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nFile ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter or map the ID of the file you want to retrieve details about.\n\nGet a File List\n\nRetrieves files and/or folders details based on the search term.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your G Suite account.\n\n\n\n\nTeam Drive\n\n\t\n\nSelect the shared drive you want to list files from.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the folder you want to list files from.\n\n\n\n\nSearch\n\n\t\n\nSelect the descriptions and contents.\n\nCustom search query Enter the Google search query term. in Make, you can translate a text in your Google Translate account.\n\nTo use the Google Translate module, you must have a Google account and billing enabled in the Google Cloud Platform. You can create an account at accounts.google.com.\n\nRefer to the Google Translate API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect Google Translate to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Translate.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Translate in Make.\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Translate\n\nBefore you establish the connection in Make you must create and configure a project in the Google Cloud Console to obtain your API key.\n\nCloud Billing\n\nYour Google account must have Cloud Billing set up in order to enable the required APIs in your project. For information regarding how to create and manage Cloud Billing, see Google's Manage your Cloud Billing account guide.\n\nCreate a Google Cloud Console project for Google Translate\n\nTo create a Google Cloud Console project:\n\nSign in to Google Cloud Platform using your Google credentials.\n\nIn the top menu, click Select a project > New project.\n\nEnter a Project name and select the Location for your project.\n\nClick Create.\n\nIn the top menu, check if your new project is selected in the Select a project dropdown. If not, select the project you just created.\n\nEnable APIs for Google Translate\n\nTo enable the required API:\n\nOpen the left navigation menu and go to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch for and enable the following API: Google Translate API.\n\nObtain your Google Translate API key\n\nTo obtain your API key:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Credentials.\n\nClick + Create credentials > API key.\n\nCopy Your API key value shown and store it in a safe place.\n\nYou will use this value in the API Key field in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Translate in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Google Translate module to your scenario, and click Create a Connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key field, enter the API key copied in the Obtain your Google Translate API key section above.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Google Translate modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Google Translate Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nTransformers\n\nTranslate a text\n\nGoogle Translate\nConnect Google Translate to Make\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Translate\nEstablish the connection with Google Translate in Make\nBuild Google Translate Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
