can create and modify notes, update permissions, and make API calls.\n\nTo use Google Keep modules, you must have a Google Cloud Platform account. If you do not have one, you can create one at console.cloud.google.com. The Google Keep API is an enterprise-only API, so you must use a Google Cloud Platform service account with domain-wide delegation enabled.\n\nRefer to the Google Keep API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nNote\n\nMake's use and transfer of information received from Google APIs to any other app will adhere to Google API Services User Data Policy.\n\nConnect Google Keep to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Keep.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Keep in Make.\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Keep\n\nBefore you establish the connection in Make, you must create and configure a project in the Google Cloud Console to obtain your client credentials.\n\nCreate a Google Cloud Console project for Google Keep\n\nTo create a Google Cloud Console project:\n\nLog in to the Google Cloud Console using your Google credentials.\n\nIn the top menu, click Select a project > New project.\n\nEnter a Project name and select the Location for your project.\n\nClick Create.\n\nIn the top menu, check if your new project is selected in the Select a project dropdown. If not, select the project you just created.\n\nEnable APIs for Google Keep\n\nTo enable the required API:\n\nOpen the left navigation menu and go to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch for and enable the following API: Google Keep API.\n\nConfigure your OAuth consent screen for Google Keep\n\nTo configure your OAuth consent screen:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click OAuth consent screen.\n\nUnder User Type, select External.\n\nFor more information regarding user types, refer to Google's Exceptions to verification requirements documentation.\n\nClick Create.\n\nFill in the required fields with your information.\n\nIn the Authorized domains section, add make.com and integromat.com.\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nIn the Scopes page, click Add or remove scopes, add the following scopes, and click Update.\n\nhttps://www.googleapis.com/auth/keep\n\nhttps://www.googleapis.com/auth/keep.readonly\n\nNote: The Google Keep API is an enterprise-only API, so you must use a Google Cloud Platform service account with domain-wide delegation enabled to use these scopes.\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nOptional: If your project will remain in the Testing publishing status, add test user emails on the Test users page, then click Save and continue.\n\nCreate your Google Keep client credentials\n\nTo create your client credentials:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Credentials.\n\nClick + Create Credentials > OAuth client ID.\n\nIn the Application type dropdown, select Web application.\n\nUpdate the Name of your OAuth client. This will help you identify it in the console.\n\nIn the Authorized redirect URIs section, click + Add URI and enter the following redirect URI: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/google-custom/\n\nCopy your Client ID and Client secret values and store them in a safe place.\n\nYou will use these values in the Client ID and Client Secret fields in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Keep in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Google Keep module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the values you copied in the Create your Google Keep client credentials section above.\n\nClick Sign in with Google.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. allow you to list, retrieve, create, update, or delete contacts, contact addresses, contact hotness, contact sources, custom fields, events, tags, campaigns, and leads in your LionDesk account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA LionDesk account\n\nIn order to use LionDesk with Make, it is necessary to have a LionDesk account. If you do not have one, you can create a LionDesk account at www.liondesk.com/freetrial.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting LionDesk to Make\n\nTo connect your LionDesk account to Make follow the general instructions for Connecting to services.\n\nAfter you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the LionDesk website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Allow button.\n\nContacts\nList Contacts\n\nRetrieves all contacts based on filter settings.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of results Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\n\n\n\nSorting Field\n\n\t\n\nSelect the field you want to sort the result by.\n\n\n\n\nOrder\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to sort result in the ascending or descending order.\n\n\n\n\nFilter: Before Date\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to enter creation or modification date.\n\n\n\n\nOrder\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether to include entered date to the filter.\n\n\n\n\nBefore Date\n\n\t\n\nEnter the date before that the contact has been created. The rank is the order of the hotness when displayed in lists. Rank of 0 will be at the top of the list.\n\n\n\n\nHotness Color\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Hex code of the color for the hotness level. E.g. #F3411B.\n\nUpdate Hotness\n\nEdits the hotness level.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nHotness ID\n\n\t\n\nMap or select the hotness you want to update.\n\nPlease find the descriptions of the fields in the Create Hotness section above.\n\nCreate/Update/Delete Contact Hotness\n\nCreates, updates, or deletes hotness from the specified contact.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nContact ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the contact you want to create, update, or delete the hotness for.\n\n\n\n\nHotness ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the hotness level you want to create or update. Delete the hotness by switching to the mapping mode and entering 0 to the field.\n\nContact Source\n\nList Sources\n\nRetrieves all lead source.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of sources Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet Source\n\nRetrieves source details.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nSource ID\n\n\t\n\nMap or select a source you want to retrieve details about.\n\nDelete Source\n\nDeletes a source.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nSource ID\n\n\t\n\nMap or select a source you want to delete.\n\nCreate Source\n\nCreates a new source\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter a name for the new source.\n\nUpdate Source\n\nChanges the name of a source.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nSource ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the source you want to rename.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter a new name of the source.\n\nCreate/Update/Delete Source\n\nCreates, updates, or deletes source from the specified contact.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your LionDesk account.\n\n\n\n\nContact ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the contact you want to create, update, or delete the source for.\n\n\n\n\nSource ID\n\n\t\n\nSelect or map the source you want to create or update. Speech modules in Make, you can retrieve the status of asynchronous speech recognition, and start asynchronous and synchronous speech recognitions.\n\nGetting Started with Google Cloud Speech\n\nPrerequisites:\n\nA Google Cloud Platform account\n\nGoogle Cloud Credentials (OAuth Client ID and Client Secret)\n\nEnabled Google Speech-to-Text service\n\nTo get started with Google Cloud Platform, create an account at Google Cloud Speech-to-text.\n\nNote\n\nMake's use and transfer of information received from Google APIs to any other app will adhere to Google API Services User Data Policy.\n\nConnect Google Cloud Speech to Make\n\nTo connect Google Cloud Speech to Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Google Cloud Speech module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the client credentials of your custom app.\n\nClick the Sign in with Google button and select your Google account.\n\nReview the access information and click Allow.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Google Cloud Speech modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nObtain client credentials for your custom app\n\nTo obtain the client credentials, you must have access to Google Cloud Console and be able to create or edit the project.\n\nSign in to Google Cloud console using your Google credentials.\n\nClick Select a project > NEW PROJECT. Enter the desired project name, and click the CREATE button.\n\nSelect the project you have created.\n\nGo to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch and enable the following required APIs:\n\nCloud Resource Manager API\n\nThe desired service option should display as you type. Select the API/service you want to connect to Make.\n\nClick the ENABLE button to enable the selected API.\n\nNavigate to APIs & Services > OAuth consent screen.\n\nChoose the External option, and click the CREATE button.\n\nNote\n\nYou will not be charged when selecting this option! For more details, please refer to Google's Exceptions to verification requirements.\n\nFill in the required fields as follows, and then click Save and Continue:\n\nApp name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name of the app asking for consent. For example,  Make.\n\n\n\n\nAuthorized domains\n\n\t\n\nmake.com\n\nintegromat.com\n\nYou don't have to set anything in the Scopes and Optional info sections. Click Save and Continue.\n\nIn the Test Users section, click ADD USERS and enter the testing user email address to access the app.\n\nNavigate to Credentials. Click the +CREATE CREDENTIALS and select the OAuth Client ID option.\n\nFill in the required fields as follows, and then click the CREATE button to create the application:\n\nApplication type\n\n\t\n\nweb application\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nName of the application. For example, Make.\n\n\n\n\nAuthorized redirect URIs\n\n\t\n\nhttps://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/google-restricted\n\nFor Google Cloud Speech, add https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/google-cloud-speech\n\nA dialog containing the app's Client ID and Client Secret is displayed. Save them in a safe place for later use.\n\nYou have successfully created the client credentials.\n\nNote\n\nIf you are using custom apps with publishing state, Testing, then you must set up the access token NOT TO be forced to re-authenticate every week after expiration.\n\nFor more information, see on setting up OAuth consent screen.\n\nTo set up app token and authentication, see using OAuth 2.0 for Web Server applications.\n\nEnable the Cloud Speech to Text Service\n\nIn order to start using the Google Cloud Speech module, it is necessary to enable the Cloud Speech-to-Text service.\n\nGo to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch for Cloud Speech-to-Text API.\n\nEnable Cloud Speech-to-Text API.\n\nActions\nSpeech: Long Running Recognize\nOperations: Get\nSearches\nSpeech: Recognize\nGoogle Cloud Speech\nGetting Started with Google Cloud Speech\nConnect Google Cloud Speech to Make\nObtain client credentials for your custom app\nEnable the Cloud Speech to Text Service\nActions\nSpeech: Long Running Recognize\nOperations: Get\nSearches\nSpeech: Recognize\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementGoogle Cloud Text-to-Speech\nGoogle Cloud Text-to-Speech\n\nWith Google Cloud Text-to-Speech modules in Make, you can convert text or Speech Synthesis Markup Language (SSML) input into audio data of natural human speech in your Google Cloud Text-to-Speech account.\n\nTo use the Google Cloud Text-to-Speech module, you must have a Google account, a project created in the Google Cloud Console, and billing enabled for the Google project. You can create an account at accounts.google.com.\n\nRefer to the Google Cloud Text-to-Speech API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nNote\n\nMake's use and transfer of information received from Google APIs to any other app will adhere to Google API Services User Data Policy.\n\nConnect Google Cloud Text-to-Speech to Make\n\nTo establish the connection, you must:\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Cloud Text-to-Speech.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Cloud Text-to-Speech in Make.\n\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Cloud Text-to-Speech.\n\nBefore you establish the connection in Make, you must create and configure a project in the Google Cloud Console to obtain your client credentials.\n\nCreate a Google Cloud Console project for Google Cloud Text-to-Speech\n\nTo create a Google Cloud Console project:\n\nLog in to the Google Cloud Console using your Google credentials.\n\nIn the top menu, click Select a project > New project.\n\nEnter a Project name and select the Location for your project.\n\nClick Create.\n\nIn the top menu, check if your new project is selected in the Select a project dropdown. If not, select the project you just created.\n\nENABLE APIS FOR GOOGLE CLOUD TEXT-TO-SPEECH\n\nTo enable to required API:\n\nOpen the left navigation menu and go to APIs & Services > Library.\n\nSearch for an enable the following API: Cloud Text-to-Speech API\n\nCONFIGURE YOUR OAUTH CONSENT SCREEN FOR GOOGLE CLOUD TEXT-TO-SPEECH\n\nTo configure your OAuth consent screen:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click OAuth consent screen.\n\nUnder User Type, select External.\n\nFor more information regarding user types, refer to Google's Exceptions to verification requirements documentation.\n\nClick Create.\n\nFill in the required fields with your information.\n\nIn the Authorized domains section, add make.com and integromat.com.\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nIn the Scopes page, click Add or remove scopes, add the following scope, and click Update: https://www.googleapis.com/auth/cloud-platform\n\nClick Save and continue.\n\nOptional: If your project will remain in the Testing publishing status, add test user emails on the Test users page, then click Save and continue.\n\nCREATE YOUR GOOGLE CLOUD TEXT-TO-SPEECH CLIENT CREDENTIALS\n\nTo create your client credentials:\n\nIn the left sidebar, click Credentials.\n\nClick + Create Credentials > OAuth client ID.\n\nIn the Application type dropdown, select Web application.\n\nUpdate the Name of your OAuth client. This will help you identify it in the console.\n\nIn the Authorized redirect URIs section, click + Add URI and enter the following redirect URI: https://www.integromat.com/oauth/cb/google-custom.\n\nCopy your Client ID and Client secret values and store them in a safe place.\n\nYou will use these values in the Client ID and Client Secret fields in Make.\n\nEstablish the connection with Google Cloud Text-to-Speech in Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a Google Cloud Text-to-Speech module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Client ID and Client Secret fields, enter the values you copied in the Create your Google Cloud Text-to-Speech client credentials section above.\n\nClick Sign in with Google.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Google Cloud Text-to-Speech modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild Google Cloud Text-to-Speech Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nSynthesis\n\nSynthesize a Speech\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nGoogle Cloud Text-to-Speech\nConnect Google Cloud Text-to-Speech to Make\nCreate and configure a Google Cloud Console project for Google Cloud Text-to-Speech.\nBuild Google Cloud Text-to-Speech Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

manage the documents, and create contacts in your GetAccept account.\n\nTo use the GetAccept modules, you must have a paid GetAccept account. You can create an account at getaccept.com. For subscription information, refer to the GetAccept Pricing page.\n\nRefer to the GetAccept API documentation for a list of available endpoints.\n\nConnect GetAccept to Make\n\nTo establish the connection in Make:\n\nLog in to your Make account, add a GetAccept module to your scenario, and click Create a connection.\n\nNote: If you add a module with an instant tag, click Create a webhook, then Create a connection.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Email and Password fields, enter your GetAccept account login credentials.\n\nClick Save.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more GetAccept modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nBuild GetAccept Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nFiles\n\nUpload a File\n\nDocuments\n\nWatch Documents Created\n\nWatch Documents Sent\n\nWatch Documents Reviewed\n\nWatch Documents Signed\n\nSearch Documents\n\nList Document Recipients\n\nGet Document Details\n\nDownload a Document\n\nCreate a Document\n\nCreate a Document from Template\n\nDelete a Document\n\nContacts\n\nCreate a Contact\n\nOther\n\nMake an API Call\n\nNote\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nWhen you create a GetAccept webhook in Make, it is attached automatically and requires no additional set up.\n\nGetAccept\nConnect GetAccept to Make\nBuild GetAccept Scenarios\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

      "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and ERPs\nCommerce\nCommunication\nCRM and Sales tools\nCustomer Support\nDatabase\nEducation\nFile and Document Management\nAdobe Acrobat Sign\nAbyssale\nBannerbear\nBidsketch\nBox\nCitrix ShareFile\nCloudConvert\nConvertAPI\nConvertio\nConverts.online\nCSV\nDeezer\nDocupilot\nDocuSign\nDropbox\nDropbox Business\nDubb\nDocuWare\nEasyCSV\nEgnyte\nEledo PDF generator\nEvernote\nFiles.com\nFlickr\nFormstack\nFormstack Documents\nFrame.io\nFTP\nGetAccept\nGIPHY\nGoogle Cloud Speech\nGoogle Cloud Text-to-Speech\nGoogle Docs\nGoogle Drive\nGoogle Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementFTP\nFTP \nGetting Started with FTP\n\nFTP modules let you monitor file changes in a selected folder, upload new files to the desired folder, and modify or delete existing files that are already in a folder.\n\nPrerequisites for FTP\n\nAn FTP server or FTP hosting (for example GoDaddy web hosting).\n\nCreating the FTP Connection\n\nConnection name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for your FTP connection.\n\n\n\n\nHost\n\n\t\n\nEnter the FTP server hostname. E.g. myftp123.server.com\n\n\n\n\nPort\n\n\t\n\nEnter the FTP server port number. E.g. 21\n\n\n\n\nUser name\n\n\t\n\nEnter your FTP account user name.\n\n\n\n\nPassword\n\n\t\n\nEnter your FTP account password.\n\n\n\n\nUse a secure connection (TLS)\n\n\t\n\nSelect if you want to use a secure connection.\n\nNo\n\nThe connection will not be secured.\n\nExplicit encryption or Implicit encryption\n\nFTPS connection. The connection will be secured using SSL.\n\n\n\n\nReject unauthorized certificates\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is enabled, the FTP server certificate is verified. If the verification fails, the connection will not be created. To pass the verification, the certificate must meet one of the following criteria:\n\nbe signed by a Root Certificate Authority\n\nbe signed by an Intermediate Certificate Authority (see e.g. How certificate chains work for further explanation). In this case all the Intermediate Certificates should be installed on the FTP server.\n\nbe a Self-Signed Certificate supplied in the Self-signed certificate field (see below)\n\nIf this option is disabled, the FTP server certificate is not verified. We strongly advise against disabling the option as it renders the connection insecure and poses a serious security risk.\n\n\n\n\nSelf-signed certificate\n\n\t\n\nClick the Extract button to open the upload dialog.\n\nUpload the certificate to use the TLS with your self-signed certificate. Make does not retain or store any data (files, passwords) you provide. File and password are only used to extract the certificate.\n\nDid you know?\n\nYou can find predefined FTP app sample templates at www.make.com/en/templates/ftp\n\nTriggers\nWatch files\n\nMonitors the file content of the selected folder. The trigger is executed when a new file is inserted into the specified folder.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the folder you want to watch.\n\nOnly one folder per scenario is allowed. Subfolders are ignored.\n\nTo keep track of multiple folders, create an independent scenario for each of them.\n\n\n\n\nMaximum number of returned files\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of results that Make will work with during one cycle. If the value is set too high, the connection may be interrupted on the side of the given third-party service (timeout). Make has no influence on this. We recommend that you set a lower value and either define a higher value for the maximum number of cycles or run the scenario more frequently.\n\nChoose where to start\n\nSet when do you want to start the FTP file monitoring from.\n\nActions\nUpload a file\n\nUploads a file to the FTP server.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the FTP folder you want to upload the file to.\n\n\n\n\nSource file\n\n\t\n\nSelect (or map) the file you want to upload to the FTP server.\n\n\n\n\nAppend to an already existing file\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is enabled and the file already exists on the FTP server, its content will be appended. If not, the content of the file will be overwritten.\n\n\n\n\nCreate folders if don't exist\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is enabled and the folder you have entered to the Folder field does not exist on the FTP server, the module will create the folder.\n\nDelete a file\n\nDeletes a file from the specified folder.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the FTP folder you want to delete a file from.\n\n\n\n\nFile name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the filename (including file name extension). E.g. image.png\n\nCreate a folder\n\nCreates a new folder.\n\nMake sure you have sufficient permissions to create a folder and/or the directory protection is disabled.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder path\n\n\t\n\nSelect the FTP folder you want to create a folder at.\n\n\n\n\nNew folder name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the new folder.\n\nDelete a folder\n\nDeletes a folder.\n\nMake sure you have sufficient permissions to delete a folder and/or the directory protection is disabled.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the FTP folder you want to delete.\n\nMove a file or folder\n\nMoves a file from one folder to another.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nOld file path\n\n\t\n\nEnter the path you want to move the file from. For example /folder1/test.txt\n\n\n\n\nNew file path\n\n\t\n\nEnter the path you want to move the file to. For example /folder2/test.txt. (The target file name can differ from the source file name.)\n\nList of files/folders in a folder\n\nRetrieves file and/or folder details.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFolder\n\n\t\n\nSelect the FTP folder you want to search in.\n\n\n\n\nShow\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to retrieve information about files or folders, or both.\n\n\n\n\nSearch\n\n\t\n\nEnter the search term to filter returned files/folders by. If no search term is entered all files and folders from the specified folder will be returned.\n\n\n\n\nMaximum number of returned files\n\n\t\n\nSet the maximum number of retrieved files by this module.\n\nGet a file\n\nRetrieves a file from the FTP server which can be further processed, e.g. attached to the email message.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nFile path\n\n\t\n\nEnter the path of the file you want to retrieve.\n\nThe Example\n\nThe file is retrieved from the FTP server and attached to the Gmail email message.\n\nChange permissions\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the FTP account.\n\n\n\n\nChange permission settings of\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to change permissions of the file or the folder.\n\n\n\n\nFile path\n\n\t\n\nEnter the folder or file path.\n\n\n\n\nPermissions\n\n\t\n\nSet the desired file/folder permissions. Use the chmod parameters. E.g. 777 or -rwxrwxrwx\n\nYou can find more details on the chmod Man Page.\n\nTroubleshooting the FTP app\n\nIf you are experiencing issues with the FTP app either during the connection creation or during a module's operation, try to use one of the popular FTP clients (e.g. WinSCP) and try to perform the same action (e.g. create a connection, list files in a folder, etc.) with the FTP client. If you are experiencing the same issues also with the FTP client, the reason might be a misconfiguration of the FTP server.\n\nPlease note that there are two FTP modes: active and passive. As the Make FTP app requests the passive mode, the FTP server must support the passive mode in order an FTP session can be successfully established during the following four steps:\n\nThe Make server sends the PASV command to the FTP server on port 21 (or 990 if Use a secure connection (TLS): \"Implicit encryption\" option has been chosen in the connection setup). This port must be open on the FTP server's firewall.\n\nThe FTP server should send 227: Entering Passive Mode (h1,h2,h3,h4,p1,p2) in response. The response specifies:\n\nThe IP address (h1, h2, h3, h4) the Make server should connect to. When the FTP server is behind a NAT, the FTP server needs to provide its external IP address. It is common that the FTP server is not configured properly and provides its internal IP address instead that cannot be connected to from the Make server, e.g.:\n\nA random, high-numbered (ephemeral) port (p1, p2) that the Make server can connect to. This port must be open on the FTP server's firewall.\n\nThe Make server initiates a connection to the IP address and port specified in the response.\n\nThe FTP server responds with an ACK. The FTP session has now been established.\n\nSources\n\nhttps://winscp.net/eng/docs/ftp_modes\n\nhttps://documentation.meraki.com/MX/NAT_and_Port_Forwarding/Active_and_Passive_FTP_Overview_and_Configuration#section_3\n\nFTP\nGetting Started with FTP\nPrerequisites for FTP\nCreating the FTP Connection\nDid you know?\nTriggers\nWatch files\nActions\nUpload a file\nDelete a file\nCreate a folder\nDelete a folder\nMove a file or folder\nList of files/folders in a folder\nGet a file\nChange permissions\nTroubleshooting the FTP app\nSources\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."
    },

Formstack Documents\n\nThe Formstack Documents modules allow you to merge the data route and merge the documents in your Formstack Documents account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA Formstack Documents account\n\nIn order to use the Formstack Document with Make, it is necessary to have a Formstack Documents account. If you do not have one, you can create a Formstack Documents account at www.formstack.com/admin/signup.\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnect Formstack Documents to Make\n\nLogin to your Formstack Documents account.\n\nClick your profile icon > API Access.\n\nEnter a name for the API and click Create API.\n\nCopy the API Key and API Secret to your clipboard.\n\nGo to Make and open the Formstack Documents module's Create a connection dialog.\n\nIn the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the API Key and API Secret fields, enter the details copied in step 4 respectively.\n\nClick Continue.\n\nThe connection has been established.\n\nActions\nMerge Data Route\nMerge Document\nInserting images in Formstack Documents via Make\n\nTo create merged documents with images (e.g. signatures) via Make, you need to know the URL to the image or the base64 representation of the image (i.e. data:image/png;base64,<BASE 64 HERE>) so that Make can pass this information to WebMerge and the image can be embedded. Evernote\n\nPrerequisites\n\nAn Evernote account\n\nIn order to use Evernote with Make, it is necessary to have an Evernote account. If you do not have one, you can create an Evernote account at evernote.com.\n\nConnecting Evernote to Make\n\nTo connect Evernote to Make you must connect your Evernote account to Make.\n\nAfter you click the Continue button, Make will redirect you to the Evernote website where you will be prompted to grant Make access to your account.\n\nConfirm the dialog by clicking the Authorize button.\n\nTemplates\n\nYou can find over 60 predefined Evernote sample templates at www.make.com/en/templates/evernote\n\nTriggers\nWatch Notes\n\nThis module is triggered when a note is created or updated in a selected notebook.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nNotebook\n\n\t\n\nSelect the notebook you want to watch for new or updated notes.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect the tags of the notes you want to retrieve.\n\n\n\n\nMaximum number of returned notes\n\n\t\n\nEnter the maximum number of notes that Make will work with during one cycle (the number of repetitions per scenario run). If the value is set too high, the connection may be interrupted on the side of the given third-party service (timeout). Make has no influence on this.\n\n\n\n\nWatch\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to retrieve new notes or new notes and all changes.\n\n\n\n\nOnly notes with reminders\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option if you want to retrieve only notes that contain a reminder.\n\nActions\nCreate a Note\n\nCreates a new note in a selected notebook.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nNotebook\n\n\t\n\nSelect the notebook you want to create a note in.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title for the note.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired note content.\n\n\n\n\nEscape HTML characters\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is disabled you must use HTML character entity, e.g.\n\n                           &amp;\n                        \n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nAdd a tag to the new note if needed.\n\n\n\n\nReminder time\n\n\t\n\nIf you want to set the reminder for this note enter the date and time for the reminder.\n\n\n\n\nAttachments\n\n\t\n\nAttach a file to the note. More information about working with files.\n\nUpdate a Note\n\nUpdates a selected note.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nNotebook\n\n\t\n\nSelect the notebook you want to update the note in.\n\n\n\n\nSelect a note\n\n\t\n\nSelect the note you want to update. If you want to enter the ID manually you can use the Watch notes module or Search for notes module to retrieve the Note ID. Otherwise, select a note from the Note drop-down menu.\n\n\n\n\nTitle\n\n\t\n\nEnter the title for the note. This field is mandatory.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired content of the note. This field is mandatory.\n\n\n\n\nEscape HTML characters\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is disabled you must use HTML character entity, e.g.\n\n                           &amp;\n                        \n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nAdd a tag to the new note if needed.\n\n\n\n\nUpdate a reminder\n\n\t\n\nChoose whether you want to Update or Clear a reminder.\n\n\n\n\nReminder time\n\n\t\n\nIf you want to set a reminder for this note enter the date and time for the reminder.\n\n\n\n\nAttachments\n\n\t\n\nAttach a file to the note. More information about working with files.\n\nAppend Content to a Note\n\nAdds content to a note.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nSelect a note\n\n\t\n\nSelect the note you want to update. If you want to enter the ID manually you can use the Watch notes module or Search for notes module to retrieve the Note ID. Otherwise, select a note from the Note drop-down menu.\n\n\n\n\nContent\n\n\t\n\nEnter the content you want to add to the note. It will be appended to the end of the note content.\n\n\n\n\nEscape HTML characters\n\n\t\n\nIf this option is disabled you must use HTML character entity, e.g.\n\n                           &amp;\n                        \n\n\n\nAttachments\n\n\t\n\nAttach a file to the note. More information about working with files.\n\nDelete a Note\n\nDeletes a selected note.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nNote ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter the Note ID. You can use, for example, the Watch notes module or Search for notes module to retrieve the ID.\n\nGet a Note\n\nRetrieves information about a selected note.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nSelect a note\n\n\t\n\nSelect a note you want to update. If you want to enter the ID manually you can use the Watch notes module or Search for notes module to retrieve the Note ID. Otherwise, select a note from the Note drop-down menu.\n\nCreate a Notebook\n\nCreates a new notebook.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nName\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name for the new notebook.\n\nSearch for Notes\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nSearch query\n\n\t\n\nEnter the search term. To perform a more detailed search, refer to Evernote's advanced search syntax.\n\n\n\n\nNotebook\n\n\t\n\nSelect the notebook you want to search for notes.\n\n\n\n\nTags\n\n\t\n\nSelect the tags of the note you want to search for.\n\n\n\n\nMaximum number of returned notes\n\n\t\n\nEnter the maximum number of notes that Make will work with during one cycle (the number of repetitions per scenario run). If the value is set too high, the connection may be interrupted on the side of the given third-party service (timeout). Make has no influence on this.\n\n\n\n\nContinue the execution of the route even if the module returns no results\n\n\t\n\nIf enabled, the scenario will not be stopped by this module.\n\nShare a Note\n\nThe module provides you with a public link to a selected note.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your Evernote account.\n\n\n\n\nSelect a note\n\n\t\n\nSelect the note you want to update. If you want to enter the ID manually you can use the Watch notes module or Search for notes module to retrieve the Note ID. Otherwise, select a note from the Note drop-down menu.\n\nIterators\nRetrieve Note Attachments\n\nExtracts attachments from a note and provides them to the following module.\n\nSource module\n\n\t\n\nSelect the source module that contains an attachment(s).\n\nExample\n\nUse the following modules to extract attachments from the Evernote note and upload it to the Dropbox folder.\n\nEvernote > Get a Note module to retrieve the note with attachments.\n\nEvernote > Retrieve Note Attachments module to iterate the attachments.\n\nDropbox > Upload a File module to upload retrieved attachments to the Dropbox folder.\n\nEvernote\nGetting Started with Evernote\nConnecting Evernote to Make\nTemplates\nTriggers\nWatch Notes\nActions\nCreate a Note\nUpdate a Note\nAppend Content to a Note\nDelete a Note\nGet a Note\nCreate a Notebook\nSearch for Notes\nShare a Note\nIterators\nRetrieve Note Attachments\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

      "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsFile and Document ManagementCSV\nCSV \nGetting started with CSV\n\nThe CSV aggregator and CSV transformer lets you create csv files and parse csv text from a received text value or a file.\n\nAggregators\nCreate CSV\n\nMerges selected text items and return them in the CSV format.\n\nThe Create CSV aggregator lets you create csv text from received text values.\n\nSource Module\n\n\t\n\nSelect the app module you are using to aggregate the fields you need.\n\n\n\n\nAggregate fields\n\n\t\n\nSelect the fields you want to aggregate from the list of available fields.\n\n\n\n\nInclude headers in the first row\n\n\t\n\nWhen selected, includes the headers in the result.\n\n\n\n\nDelimiter\n\n\t\n\nSelect the delimiter character to separate the values. If you select Other, a Delimiter character field will populate below where you can specify the character.\n\n\n\n\nDelimiter character\n\n\t\n\nSpecify which delimiter character is used to separate the values if you selected Other. It must be only one character.\n\n\n\n\nNewline\n\n\t\n\nSelect the newline that is used to indicate the end of a line of text.\n\n\n\n\nGroup by\n\n\t\n\nEnter the filter to group the results. For example, a date.\n\n\n\n\nStop processing after an empty aggregation\n\n\t\n\nWhen selected, the scenario stops when there are no results.\n\nExample - Export Google Contacts to a CSV File\n\nThe Create CSV module provides you with a list of options as checkboxes. If you are selecting Contact's ID and Full Name, then the results are returned in a text format.\n\nCreate CSV (advanced)\n\nMerges selected text items and return them in the CSV format. Employs Data Structure to define CSV columns in the resulting CSV file.\n\nThe Create CSV (advanced) aggregator lets you create a csv text from received text values. It employs a Data structure that defines the CSV columns in the resulting CSV file. Once defined, the columns appear as fields in the CSV module setup, available for mapping.\n\nSource Module\n\n\t\n\nSelect the app module you are using to aggregate the fields you need.\n\n\n\n\nData Structure\n\n\t\n\nSelect the data structure to aggregate the fields in the way you want. See Adding a Data Structure.\n\nAfter defining the data structure, you can map the items to the corresponding fields.\n\n\n\n\nAggregate Fields\n\n\t\n\nProvides a list of fields you want to aggregate.\n\n\n\n\nInclude headers in the first row\n\n\t\n\nWhen selected, includes headings in the first row.\n\n\n\n\nDelimiter\n\n\t\n\nSelect the delimiter character to separate the values. If you select Other, a Delimiter character field will populate below where you can specify the character.\n\n\n\n\nDelimiter character\n\n\t\n\nSpecify which delimiter character is used to separate the values if you selected Other. It must be only one character.\n\n\n\n\nNewline\n\n\t\n\nSelect the newline that is used to indicate the end of a line of text.\n\n\n\n\nGroup by\n\n\t\n\nEnter the filter to group the results. For example, a date.\n\n\n\n\nStop processing after an empty aggregation\n\n\t\n\nWhen selected, the scenario stops when there are no results.\n\nExample - Export Google Contacts to a CSV File\n\nThe Create CSV (advanced) module provides you with the option to create a data structure with the aggregating fields you needed. If you are defining a data structure with Full Name and Email then the results are returned in a text format.\n\nTransformers\nParse CSV\n\nParses a CSV file.\n\nThe Parse CSV transformer lets you parse a csv text from a received text value or a file. If your data comes in binary form (typically from a file), you have to use the toString() function to convert the binary data to String:\n\nTransforming complex data to CSV\n\nFor example, you would like to export your Google contacts to a CSV file with two columns \"Full Name\" and \"Email\". The output bundle from the Google Contacts > Get contacts from a group module has the following structure (see on the right). The email addresses are stored inside the Emails[] item, which is an array of collections, each collection containing two items: Label and Email.\n\nIf you employ the simple Create CSV module, you are offered a list of checkboxes corresponding to a bundle's top-level items. If you attempt to tick Full name and Emails items, the Create CSV module will produce the following output, which is probably not what you wished for:\n\n \"emails\",\"fullName\"\n\"[object Object]\",\"Shon Winer\"\n\"[object Object]\",\"Lizeth Fulmore\"\n\"[object Object]\",\"Hilario Gullatt\"\n\"[object Object]\",\"Abby Eisenbarth\"\n         \n\nSince the item Full Name is of simple type text it is exported just fine. But the item Emails, which is of a complex type array of collections, is exported as [object Object]. That is how Collections and Arrays are transformed to text by default.\n\nTo export content of the Email item of the first collection of the Emails[] array instead, it is necessary to employ the Create CSV (advanced) module. The module will enable you to define individual columns of your CSV file and map items to them, including the nested ones.\n\n1. Insert the module Create CSV (advanced) in a scenario and open its configuration.\n\n2. Click the Add button next to the Data structure field to create a new Data structure.\n\n3. Input a name for the Data structure and click the Add item button to add the individual columns. If you wish to export two columns: \"Full Name\" and \"Email\", the resulting Data structure would look like this:\n\n4. Once you have successfully defined the Data structure, fields corresponding to each individual column should appear in the configuration of the Create CSV (advanced) module so you can map the items. Take the first item from the Emails[] array and map its item Email to the field/column Email:\n\n5. Execute the scenario. CloudConvert modules allow you to monitor and manage jobs, tasks, and import&export files in your CloudConvert account.\n\nPrerequisites\n\nA CloudConvert account\n\nIn order to use CloudConvert with Make, it is necessary to have a CloudConvert account. If you do not have one, you can create a CloudConvert account at cloudconvert.com/register.\n\nCaution\n\nThe module dialog fields that are displayed in bold (in the Make scenario, not in this documentation article) are mandatory!\n\nConnecting CloudConvert to Make\n\nTo connect your CloudConvert account to Make you need to obtain the API Key from your CloudConvert account and insert it in the Create a connection dialog in the Make module.\n\n1. Log in to your CloudConvert account and open your Dashboard.\n\n2. Open the Authorization > API Keys section.\n\n3. Click on the Create New API key button.\n\n4. Enter the name for the API key, enable the scopes you want to use, and click the Create button.\n\n5. Copy the provided token and store it in a safe place.\n\n6. Go to Make and open the CloudConvert module's Create a connection dialog.\n\n7. Enter the token you have created in step 5 and click the Continue button to establish the connection.\n\nCommon Tasks\nConvert a File\n\nConverts a specified file to the selected file format.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nInput File\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to upload a file using Make or provide the URL the file will be uploaded from.\n\n\n\n\nUpload a File\n\n\t\n\nEnter the source file by adding the file name and file data manually or by mapping the file from a previous module. E.g. Dropbox > Get a File.\n\nData\n\nEnter or map the file data.\n\nFile Name\n\nEnter the file name including the file extension. E.g. test.txt\n\n\n\n\nImport a File from URL\n\n\t\n\nURL\n\nEnter the URL of the file you want to convert.\n\nHeaders\n\nDefine request headers (optional). Useful, for example, when the specified URL requires the authorization.\n\n\n\n\nFormat\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to specify the input format of the file you want to convert. If not specified, the extension of the input file is used as the input format.\n\n\n\n\nInput Format\n\n\t\n\nSelect the current format of the file.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Format\n\n\t\n\nSelect the target file format you want to convert the file to.\n\n\n\n\nFile Name\n\n\t\n\nChoose a filename (including extension) for the target output file.\n\n\n\n\nConversion and engine specific options\n\n\t\n\nSpecify conversion and engine specific options. To view available options, please visit their API documentation and select the input_format and output_format.\n\n\n\n\nDownload a file\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to include also file data in the module's output.\n\nCapture a Website\n\nCaptures a specified website and saves it in PDF, JPG, or PNG format.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter the URL of the website you want to capture.\n\n\n\n\nOutput Format\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether you want to save the captured website in PNG, JPG, or PDF format.\n\n\n\n\nFile Name\n\n\t\n\nEnter a filename (including extension) for the target output file.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nDefine request headers (optional). To view available options, please visit their API documentation and select the output_format.\n\n\n\n\nDownload a File\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to include also file data in the module's output.\n\nJobs\nNew Job Event\n\nTriggers when the job or task is created, has finished, or has failed in your account.\n\nNote\n\nThe job created by the Create a Job (advanced) module consists of several tasks.\n\nCaution\n\nThe New Job Event trigger is also triggered when an individual task is created, has finished, or has failed.\n\nWebhhook name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the webhook name. E.g. Document Conversion Finished\n\n\n\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nEvent\n\n\t\n\nSelect whether the module is triggered when the job/task is created, has finished, or has failed.\n\nCreate a Job (advanced)\n\nThis module performs a job (a job can be one or multiple tasks that are identified in the Name field and linked between each other using the Input field).\n\nCaution\n\nFor further processing of the finished job created with the Create a Job module, please use the New Job Event (job.finished) module in another scenario.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nInput Files\n\n\t\n\nAdd the files you want to use within the job.\n\nUpload a File\n\n\t\n\nEnter the source file by adding the file name and file data manually or by mapping the file from a previous module. E.g. Dropbox > Get a File.\n\nData\n\nEnter or map the file data.\n\nFile Name\n\nEnter the file name including the file extension. E.g. test.txt\n\n\n\n\nImport a file from URL\n\n\t\n\nURL\n\nEnter the URL of the file you want to process.\n\nHeaders\n\nDefine request headers (optional). Useful, for example, when the specified URL requires the authorization.\n\n\n\n\nTasks\n\n\t\n\nAdd tasks that will be performed within the job.\n\nPlease find the descriptions of the operations' fields in the corresponding section.\n\nConvert a File\n\nCapture a Website\n\nOptimize a File\n\nMerge Files\n\nCreate Archives\n\nExecute a Command (CloudConvert API Documentation)\n\nExport a File to Temporary URL (specify the task name and input task name (e.g. Conversion)).\n\n\n\n\nTag\n\n\t\n\nAn arbitrary string to identify the job. Does not have any effect and can be used to associate the job with an ID.\n\nIf working with the Array Aggregator (e.g. you have many files in different formats to convert), use the I don't know the input format option in the Add a task dialog. Otherwise the error is returned.\n\nLinking tasks within the job (name > input, name > input,...):\n\nList Jobs\n\nRetrieves all jobs that have been run in your account.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nStatus\n\n\t\n\nSelect the job status to filter returned jobs by.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the number of returned jobs Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nGet a Job\n\nRetrieves job details.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nJob ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the job you want to retrieve details about.\n\nDelete a Job\n\nDeletes a job, including all tasks and data.\n\nJobs are deleted automatically 24 hours after they have ended.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nJob ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the job you want to delete.\n\nTasks\nGet a Task\n\nRetrieves task details.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the task you want to retrieve details about.\n\nDownload a File\n\nRetrieves file name and file data from the specified task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the task you want to download the file from.\n\nList Tasks\n\nRetrieves all tasks in your account based on filter settings.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nStatus\n\n\t\n\nSelect the task status to filter returned tasks by.\n\n\n\n\nJob ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the Job ID to return only tasks within the specified job.\n\n\n\n\nOperation\n\n\t\n\nEnter the operation type to return only tasks with the specified operation. Use the List Possible Operations module to retrieve operations.\n\n\n\n\nLimit\n\n\t\n\nSet the number of returned tasks Make will return during one execution cycle.\n\nRetry a Task\n\nCreates a new task, based on the settings (payload) of another task.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the task you want to create a new task from.\n\nCancel Task\n\nCancels a task that has a status of waiting or processing.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the task you want to cancel.\n\nDelete a Task\n\nDelete a task, including all data.\n\nTasks are deleted automatically 24 hours after they have ended.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nTask ID\n\n\t\n\nEnter (map) the ID of the task you want to delete.\n\nOther\nGet My Info\n\nRetrieves authenticated account details (including credits - remaining conversion minutes).\n\nMake an API Call\n\nAllows you to perform a custom API call.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to your CloudConvert account.\n\n\n\n\nURL\n\n\t\n\nEnter a path relative to https://api.cloudconvert.com/. For example: /v2/tasks\n\nFor the list of available endpoints, refer to the CloudConvert API v2 Documentation.\n\n\n\n\nMethod\n\n\t\n\nSelect the HTTP method you want to use:\n\nGET - to retrieve information for an entry.\n\nPOST - to create a new entry.\n\nPUT - to update/replace an existing entry.\n\nPATCH - to make a partial entry update.\n\nDELETE - to delete an entry.\n\n\n\n\nHeaders\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired request headers. You don't have to add authorization headers; we already did that for you.\n\n\n\n\nQuery String\n\n\t\n\nEnter the request query string.\n\n\n\n\nBody\n\n\t\n\nEnter the body content for your API call.\n\nExample of Use - List Tasks\n\nThe following API call returns all tasks from your CloudFront account:\n\nURL:\n\n/v2/tasks\n\nMethod:\n\nGET\n\nMatches of the search can be found in the module's Output under Bundle > Body > data.\n\nIn our example, 6 tasks were returned:\n\nTroubleshooting\n\nThe CloudConvert > Convert a File throws one of the following errors:\n\nError\n\nThe output file size exceeds the limit allowed for your scenario.\n\nPlease refer to file size limits in Working with files.\n\nError\n\nYou have exceeded the maximum conversion time.\n\nThe free CloudConvert plan offers 25 conversion minutes daily. If your usage exceeds the limit of the free plan, you may switch to a (prepaid) package or subscription.\n\nError\n\nFailed to read frame size: Could not seek to 1508. �/output/JLIADSA00137P0.mp3: Invalid argument.\n\nThis error is thrown e.g. when converting files from MP3 to WAV. Make sure that you have selected the correct region because it will find references to files but not only just the correct file.\n\nRuntimeError\n\nMaximum number of repeats exceeded.\n\nLocate the corresponding CloudConvert job in your CloudConvert dashboard's list of jobs and check the job's duration:\n\nThe CloudConvert > Convert a File module's timeout is set to 3 minutes. If the job's duration exceeds 3 minutes (possibly due to a temporary overload of the CloudConvert service), the module throws the above mentioned error.\n\nIn this case consider one of these options:\n\nEnable the Allow storing of Incomplete Executions option in the scenario settings to store the incomplete executions for later manual resolution. Optionally you may attach an error handling route to the CloudConvert module with the Break directive to resolve the incomplete executions automatically.\n\nDisable the Download a file option in the CloudConvert > Convert a file module. In this case the module will not wait for the conversion result. To obtain the conversion result, create a new scenario and use the CloudConvert > New Job Event trigger.\n\nExample: Converting a video from MOV to MP4 format\n\nVisit https://cloudconvert.com/video-converter\n\nClick on the \"Select File\" button and choose your sample MOV file.\n\nClick on the dropdown, next to \"Convert to\" and choose MP4.\n\nClick on the wrench icon.\n\nConfigure the MP4 compression settings as you see fit.\n\nClick on the Convert button.\n\nOnce the conversion has been finished, click on the Download button.\n\nReview the converted video.\n\nRepeat steps 1 to 8 until you have found the optimal conversion settings in step 5.\n\nVisit https://cloudconvert.com/api/v2/convert#convert-tasks\n\nChoose 'mov' for the input_format field.\n\nChoose 'mp4' for the output_format field.\n\nA list of all possible parameters like video_codec, crf, etc. will appear.\n\nIn Make, insert the CloudConvert > Convert a File module in your scenario.\n\nOpen the module's settings.\n\nConfigure the module as shown below:\n\nMake sure to include all the settings in the Conversion and engine specific options field: for each setting from step 5, locate the corresponding parameter from step 13 and its corresponding value.\n\nCloudConvert\nGetting Started with CloudConvert\nConnecting CloudConvert to Make\nCommon Tasks\nConvert a File\nCapture a Website\nOptimize a File\nCreate an Archive\nMerge Files\nJobs\nNew Job Event\nCreate a Job (advanced)\nList Jobs\nGet a Job\nDelete a Job\nTasks\nGet a Task\nDownload a File\nList Tasks\nRetry a Task\nCancel Task\nDelete a Task\nOther\nGet My Info\nMake an API Call\nExample of Use - List Tasks\nTroubleshooting\nExample: Converting a video from MOV to MP4 format\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

This is used to uniquely identify files that have the same name. Drag and place the Increment function module between the Box Upload a File module and the Ignore error handler module.\n\nOnce done, configure the module.\n\nClone the Upload a file module so that you do not have to remap it. Add the cloned Upload a file module in between the Increment function module and the Ignore error handler module.\n\nYou can configure the cloned Upload a file module to include the file name with the extension. For example, invoice.xml.\n\nBox\nConnect Box to Make\nBuild Box Scenarios\nTroubleshooting\nWatch files trigger did not download a file contained in the folder\nUnable to upload or update a file\nTips\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

generate visuals and manage the scaling, export, and retrieval of visuals in your Abyssale account.\n\nTo use the Abyssale modules, you must have an Abyssale account. You can now edit your scenario and add more Abyssale modules. If your connection requires reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nSet Up Abyssale Webhooks\n\nThis app uses webhooks to trigger a scenario when an event occurs instantly. All webhook modules have an instant tag next to their name.\n\nTo set up a webhook, follow these steps:\n\nAdd an Abyssale instant module to your scenario and click Create a webhook.\n\nOptional: Enter a name for the webhook in the Webhook name field.\n\nSelect the corresponding connection for the webhook in the Connection field.\n\nIf prompted, authenticate your account and confirm access.\n\nThe following message will appear when a webhook has been successfully created: We read your mind, we attached this webhook automatically for you.\n\nAbyssale will now send data to Make through the webhook when the selected event occurs.\n\nBuild Abyssale Scenarios\n\nAfter connecting the app, you can perform the following actions:\n\nActions\n\nNote: There are 2 types of available actions: synchronous (the generated visual will be returned in the response payload) and asynchronous (the notification containing the generated visual will be published at a later time). Make loads interface of input/output parameters and record set dynamically so each parameter/value can be mapped individually.\n\nBefore you start configuring your scenario, make sure the account you're using to connect to your database has read access to INFORMATION_SCHEMA.ROUTINES and INFORMATION_SCHEMA.PARAMETERS views.\n\nSupported Versions: SQL Server 2012/2014/2016/2017/2019/2022\n\nTo learn more about creating a stored procedure, see Microsoft SQL Server documentation.\n\nNotes\n\nMake does not support multiple record sets, only the first one is processed.\n\nIf SSL encryption is enabled, a valid SSL certification must be obtained. For more details, refer to the Microsoft SSL Configuration Guide.\n\nTroubleshooting Microsoft SQL Server\nER_LOCK_WAIT_TIMEOUT: Lock wait timeout exceeded; try restarting transaction\n\nThis error occurs when you modify the same data using multiple modules. It is caused by SQL transactions.\n\nWhen any SQL module is executed then it starts the transaction (1) and the transaction is finished after the scenario is fully executed. If another module tries to access the same data used in another unfinished transaction (1) then it has to wait until the previous transaction (1) is finished – but it never happens because the first transaction (1) will be finished after the scenario is finished.\n\nSolution\n\nTurn on Auto-commit. It finishes (commits) every transaction immediately after the module execution is done.\n\n1. Open Scenario settings.\n\n2. Enable the Auto commit checkbox.\n\n3. Confirm the settings dialog by clicking the OK button.\n\nMicrosoft SQL Server\nGetting started with Microsoft SQL Server (MSSQL)\nNotes\nTroubleshooting Microsoft SQL Server\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Make loads interface of input and output parameters dynamically so each parameter can be mapped individually.\n\nFunctions\n\nHere is a sample SQL statement that creates a function that just simply inserts the values passed in the three parameters into a table:\n\nCREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION insert_record_from_Make(_name character varying,_email character varying, _phone character varying)\nRETURNS void \nLANGUAGE 'plpgsql'\nAS $BODY$\nBEGIN\nINSERT INTO contacts (name, email, phone) VALUES (_name, _email, _phone);\nEND;\n$BODY$;\n\n\nTo learn more about creating functions, see PostgreSQL documentation.\n\nConfiguring your PostgreSQL server\n\nMake sure the account you're using to connect to your database has read access to 'information_schema.routines' and 'information_schema.parameters' tables.\n\nMake will make connections to your database from specifc IP addresses. Our servers are set up with valid PTR records so you can easily restrict access by allowing %.make.com.\n\nTroubleshooting PostgreSQL\nER_LOCK_WAIT_TIMEOUT: Lock wait timeout exceeded; try restarting transaction\n\nThis error occurs when you modify the same data using multiple modules. It is caused by SQL transactions.\n\nWhen any SQL module is executed then it starts the transaction (1) and the transaction is finished after the scenario is fully executed.If another module tries to access the same data used in another unfinished transaction (1) then it has to wait until the previous transaction (1) is finished – but it never happens because the first transaction (1) will be finished after the scenario is finished.\n\nSolution\n\nTurn on Auto-commit. It finishes (commits) every transaction immediately after the module execution is done.\n\nOpen Scenario settings.\n\nEnable the Auto commit checkbox.\n\nConfirm the settings dialog by clicking the OK button.\n\nPostgreSQL\nGetting started with PostgreSQL\nFunctions\nConfiguring your PostgreSQL server\nTroubleshooting PostgreSQL\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

      "title": "MySQL",
      "url": "https://www.make.com/en/help/apps/database/mysql",
      "html": "Skip to main content\nMake Help Center\nRelease notes\nGeneral\nAI in Make\nAccess management\nConnections\nScenarios\nTutorials\nModules\nMapping\nTools\nFunctions\nErrors\nDevices\nApps\nIntroduction to Make apps\nAI\nBuilt-in apps\nBusiness Intelligence\nBusiness Operations and ERPs\nCommerce\nCommunication\nCRM and Sales tools\nCustomer Support\nDatabase\nAirtable\nAmazon Redshift\nBringData.co\nCaspio\nData24-7\nGoogle Cloud Firestore\nKnack\nMySQL\nNinox\nPostgreSQL\nMicrosoft SQL Server\nTadabase\nuProc\nWasabi\nEducation\nFile and Document Management\nHR management\nInternet of Things\nIT and Development\nLanguage Tools\nLifestyle\nMarketing\nProductivity\nProcess Management\nSurveys and Forms\nTravel\nWebsite Building\nGlossary\nCommunity\nSupport\nAcademy\nBlog\nAPI documentation\nmake.com\nMake Help CenterAppsDatabaseMySQL\nMySQL \n\nThe Make MySQL modules let you execute your custom logic directly in your database server through stored procedures. Make loads the interface of input/output parameters and recordsets dynamically, so each parameter/value can be mapped individually.\n\nPreprequisites:\n\nA MySQL server connection\n\nA Configured MySQL server\n\nCreating a Connection to the MySQL Server\n\nConnection name\n\n\t\n\nEnter the name of the new MySQL connection you want to establish.\n\n\n\n\nHost\n\n\t\n\nEnter the address of the MySQL server.\n\nThe MySQL server must be publicly accessible from the internet. If you want to use the database hosted on your local server, you'll need to specify your public IP address, and set the port forwarding on your router. Do not enter \"localhost,\" or \"127.0.0.1\" in this field, as it will not work.\n\n\n\n\nPort\n\n\t\n\nEnter the port number of the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nDatabase\n\n\t\n\nEnter the database name if needed. This is required for the Execute a Query (advanced) module.\n\n\n\n\nUser\n\n\t\n\nEnter the MySQL server user name.\n\n\n\n\nPassword\n\n\t\n\nEnter the password.\n\n\n\n\nAllow insecure authentication\n\n\t\n\nEnable this option to connect to MySQL instances that use the old authentication method (MySQL 4.0 and older). If needed, see additional information about Updating Old Authentication Protocol Passwords.\n\n\n\n\nCharset\n\n(optional)\n\n\t\n\nEnter the MySQL character set for the connection, e.g., utf8. In this case, the utf8_general_ci MySQL collation is used.\n\n\n\n\nSelf-signed certificate (optional)\n\n\t\n\nUpload your certificate (P12, PFX, or PEM file) if you want to use TLS using your self-signed certificate. If you're using the client-side certificate authorization, you can enter your CA certificate here. Make does not retain or store any data (files, passwords) you provide. File and password are only used to extract a private key/certificate.\n\n\n\n\nClient Private Key (optional)\n\n\t\n\nUpload the private key to use the client-side certificate authorization. Make does not retain or store any data (files, passwords) you provide. File and password are only used to extract a private key/certificate.\n\n\n\n\nClient Certificate (optional)\n\n\t\n\nUpload your certificate if you want to use client-side certificate authorization. Make does not retain or store any data (files, passwords) you provide. File and password are only used to extract a private key/certificate.\n\nConfiguring Your MySQL Server\nCaution\n\nRemote access must be allowed, and CREATE ROUTINE privilege must be granted on the MySQL server!\n\nRead Access to MySQL Tables\n\nBefore you start configuring your scenario, ensure the account you are using to connect to your database has read access to information_schema.tables, information_schema.columns, information_schema.routines, and information_schema.parameters tables.\n\nMake IP Addresses\n\nMake will make connections to your database from the following IP addresses.\n\nOur servers are set up with valid PTR records, so you can easily restrict access by allowing %.make.com.\n\nEnabling Access on Your Firewall\n\nEnable incoming TCP connections to port 3306 from source IP addresses.\n\nConfiguring MySQL for Remote Access\n\nLinux\n\n1. Open the configuration file /etc/mysql/my.cnf\n\n2. Comment outline bind-address = 127.0.0.1 (by adding a hash at the beginning of the line):\n\n#bind-address = 127.0.0.1\n\n3. Restart the MySQL daemon\n\nCreating and Granting Remote Access to Your MySQL Account\n\n1. Start the MySQL command-line interface:\n\nmysql -u root -p\n\n2. Execute these commands (with <database>, <user> and <password> replaced by actual values):\n\nCREATE USER &lt;user&gt;@'%' IDENTIFIED BY &lt;password&gt; GRANT ALL PRIVILEGES ON &lt;database&gt;.* TO &lt;user&gt;@'%' IDENTIFIED BY &lt;password&gt; WITH GRANT OPTION; FLUSH PRIVILEGES;\n\nTolerance of Non-interactive Connection\n\nMake processes scenarios transactionally. That's why all Make modules that support transactions (e.g., MySQL) have open transactions throughout the whole run of a scenario. Therefore, make sure that you have set a long enough time to tolerate non-interactive connections. This MySQL command will list the values:\n\nSHOW VARIABLES LIKE 'wait_timeout';\n\nSee more information in the MySQL documentation on Server System Variables.\n\nConnect With MySQL Hosted From DigitalOcean:\nClick Here to follow the documentation.\nActions\nInsert Row Into a Table\n\nInserts a row with the desired values into a selected table.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table where you want to add a row.\n\n\n\n\ncolumn name(s)\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired values that will be inserted into the new row.\n\nNote\n\nTo pass a NULL value, use an INSERT statement via Execute a query (advanced) module. For more information, refer to Passing NULL Values into a Table.\n\nUpdate Row(s) in a Table\n\nUpdates rows (can be defined by the filter settings) in the selected table.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table where you want to update a row.\n\n\n\n\ncolumn name(s)\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired values that will be inserted into the rows.\n\n\n\n\nFilter\n\n\t\n\nSet the filter to define which rows will be updated.\n\nNote\n\nTo pass a NULL value, use an UPDATE statement via Execute a query (advanced) module. For more information, refer to Passing NULL Values into a Table\n\nDelete Row(s) From a Table\n\nDeletes a row according to a defined filter.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table where you want to delete the row.\n\n\n\n\nFilter\n\n\t\n\nSet the filter for the row to be deleted.\n\nSet filter values. You can also use logical operators, AND/OR, to specify your selection.\n\nPassing NULL Values into a Table\n\nAs of now, it is not possible to pass NULL values in our standard modules, Insert/Update row(s) into a table even using the null pill.\n\nTo achieve this, you need to use the Execute a query (advanced) module where you prepare a full SQL statement (either INSERT or UPDATE) as a workaround as shown in the example.\n\nYou need to update an existing row in your database with three columns: Name, Email, and Phone Number.\n\nYou want to update a contact and set the contact's phone to NULL based on the contact’s email address.\n\nTo achieve that, use this statement:\n\n`UPDATE yourtablenamehereSET Name='Joe Doe',Email='joe@doe.com',Phone=NULLWHERE Email='joe@doe.com'`\n\nIn your real scenario, map the email address (and the name possibly too) from preceding modules and ensure the mapped pills are in single quotes.\n\nExecute a Query (Advanced)\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nQuery\n\n\t\n\nEnter the desired MySQL query. Make sure that the Database field under Connection settings is filled.\n\nVariables used in the query are not sanitized. Make sure you sanitize variables properly to prevent SQL injection.\n\n\n\n\nContinue the execution of the route even if the module returns no results\n\n\t\n\nIf enabled, the scenario will not be stopped by this module.\n\nOnly one SQL statement is allowed (one semicolon ; as a statement terminator per query).\n\nExecute a Stored Procedure\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nStored procedure\n\n\t\n\nSelect the stored procedure you want to execute. The stored procedure must already be created.\n\nHere is a sample SQL statement that creates a stored procedure that simply inserts the values passed in the three parameters into a table:\n\nDELIMITER ;; CREATE PROCEDURE `insert_record_from_integromat`(IN _name text, IN _email text, IN _phone text)\n\nBEGIN INSERT INTO contacts (name, email, phone) VALUES (_name, _email, _phone); END;;\n\n\n\n\nFields\n\n\t\n\nContains the parameter fields from the stored procedure. E.g., enter values you want to insert into the table during the stored procedure execution.\n\nExample\n\nThe following example adds 2 to the provided parameter (e.g., in the Execute a Stored Procedure module), and returns the result, together with the current date (can be further iterated using the Iterate Recordset of a Stored Procedure module).\n\nCREATE PROCEDURE `test_procedure`(IN id integer, OUT outid integer)\nBEGIN\n set outid = id + 2;\n select id as inid, now() as current_date;\nEND$$\nSearches\nSelect Row(s) From a Table\n\nThis action selects a row from a table according to a defined filter.\n\nConnection\n\n\t\n\nEstablish a connection to the MySQL server.\n\n\n\n\nTable\n\n\t\n\nSelect the table you want to select a row from.\n\n\n\n\nFilter\n\n\t\n\nSet the filter for the row to be selected.\n\nSet filter values. You can also use logical operators, AND/OR, to specify your selection.\n\nExample:\n\nOn the following MySQL dialog, the row that contains number 1 or 2 in the \"column1\" column will be selected.\n\n\n\n\nContinue the execution of the route even if the module returns no results\n\n\t\n\nIf enabled, the scenario will not be stopped by this module.\n\nNote\n\nYou may also use the existing basic text operators for comparing dates and datetimes. Just use text formatted date/datetime as the second operand:\n\nYYYY-MM-DD for date type\n\nYYYY-MM-DD HH:mm:ss for datetime type\n\nLiteral static datetime value example:\n\nFormatted dynamic datetime value example:\n\nIterators\nIterates Recordset of a Stored Procedure.\n\nSource module\n\n\t\n\nSelect the source module containing the stored procedure recordset you want to iterate.\n\nTroubleshooting MySQL\nError: ER_NOT_SUPPORTED_AUTH_MODE: Client does not support authentication protocol requested by server; consider upgrading MySQL client:\n\nMySQL 8 uses an authentication method that is not supported by Make yet.\n\nSolution\n\nUse the mysql_native_password plugin to make the account fall back to the \"traditional\" process during the handshake, keeping compatibility by default for any previously supported server version.\n\nCreate the account using the mysql_native_password authentication plugin:\n\nCREATE USER 'new_user'@'%' IDENTIFIED WITH mysql_native_password BY 'user_password';\n\nOr, modify the existing user account, and specify the mysql_native_password authentication plugin:\n\nALTER USER 'root'@'localhost' IDENTIFIED WITH mysql_native_password BY 'YourRootPassword';\n\n(Reference: https://github.com/mysqljs/mysql/issues/2046#issuecomment-396039909)\n\nError: ER_LOCK_WAIT_TIMEOUT: Lock wait timeout exceeded; try restarting transaction:\n\nThis error occurs when you modify the same data using multiple modules. It is caused by SQL transactions.\n\nWhen any SQL module is executed, then it starts the transaction (1), and the transaction is finished after the scenario is fully executed. If another module tries to access the same data used in another unfinished transaction (1), then it has to wait until the previous transaction (1) is finished. This, however, never happens because the first transaction (1) will be finished when the scenario is finished.\n\nSolution\n\nTurn on Auto-commit. It finishes (commits) every transaction immediately after the module execution is done.\n\n1. Open Scenario settings.\n\n2. Enable the Auto commit checkbox.\n\n3. Confirm the settings dialog by clicking the OK button.\n\nMySQL\nCreating a Connection to the MySQL Server\nConfiguring Your MySQL Server\nRead Access to MySQL Tables\nMake IP Addresses\nEnabling Access on Your Firewall\nConfiguring MySQL for Remote Access\nCreating and Granting Remote Access to Your MySQL Account\nTolerance of Non-interactive Connection\nConnect With MySQL Hosted From DigitalOcean:\nClick Here to follow the documentation.\nActions\nInsert Row Into a Table\nUpdate Row(s) in a Table\nDelete Row(s) From a Table\nPassing NULL Values into a Table\nExecute a Query (Advanced)\nExecute a Stored Procedure\nExample\nSearches\nSelect Row(s) From a Table\nIterators\nIterates Recordset of a Stored Procedure.\nTroubleshooting MySQL\nError: ER_NOT_SUPPORTED_AUTH_MODE: Client does not support authentication protocol requested by server; consider upgrading MySQL client:\nError: ER_LOCK_WAIT_TIMEOUT: Lock wait timeout exceeded; try restarting transaction:\nPrev\nNext\n© 2024 Celonis Inc."

Copy the Application ID and API key to a safe place.\n\nIn your Make account, insert a Knack module in your scenario and click the Add button next to the Connection field.\n\nOptional: In the Connection name field, enter a name for the connection.\n\nIn the Application ID and API Key fields, enter the details copied in Step 3. In the Private API server domain field, enter the private Knack server domain if needed and click Save.\n\nYou have successfully established the connection. You can now edit your scenario and add more Knack modules. If your connection needs reauthorization at any point, follow the connection renewal steps here.\n\nTriggers\nNew Event\nWatch Records\nActions\nCreate a Record\nDelete a Record\nGet a Record\nUpdate a Record\nUpload a File\nMake an API Call\nSearches\nSearch for Records\nPrivate Knack Servers\n\nMake will make connections to your database from its IP addresses.
